  - E2E walk extension: after the M4 leg-2 (decrease, current_qty=75), workshop deep-links to `/detail`. Asserts: heading contains "Casting alloy", current_qty=75.0000, open_value contains "197.5" (= 55 × 2.50 + 20 × 3.00), 2 cost-layer rows, 4 timeline rows, 2 layer-breakdown blocks (one for OUT, one for adjust-decrease — IN and adjust-increase don't get one), pagination-single-page visible, in-link visible, edit-link absent (workshop role).

**Manual adjustment route (M4):** `app/movements.py` gains two more routes mounted under `/admin/items` for **Manager + Office + Workshop**: `GET /admin/items/{item_id}/adjust` renders an adjust form (qty + direction + unit_cost + reason + note) plus the same recent-movements + open-value summary used by stock-out; `POST /admin/items/{item_id}/adjust` validates, builds a `StockMovement(type=ADJUSTMENT)`, flushes, **dispatches on direction**: `increase` calls `record_receipt(..., source=CostLayerSource.POSITIVE_ADJUSTMENT, received_at=now())` (creates a layer + bumps qty); `decrease` calls `consume_fifo(...)` (writes consumption rows + decrements qty). Either path writes a single `stock_movement.adjustment` audit row, commits, and 303s back with a flash. The decrease path inherits M3's atomic-on-raise insufficient-stock contract verbatim — `InsufficientStockError` caught, `db.rollback()` drops the orphan movement, item reloaded via `_get_item_or_404`, form re-rendered at HTTP 400 with `<p data-testid="stock-adjust-error">Not enough stock: requested {N}, only {M} available.</p>` block + qty / direction / unit_cost / reason / note all preserved.

- **Two new helpers** (added near the existing `_parse_*` helpers): `_parse_required_reason(raw) -> str` (strip; blank → 400 — distinct from M2 / M3 where reason is optional, because MISSION §3 requires variance attribution); `_parse_direction(raw) -> str` (must be `"increase"` or `"decrease"` — anything else 400). New `_render_stock_adjust_form` factors GET-and-error rendering symmetric with M3's `_render_stock_out_form` (the same parametric error path on the only data-dependent failure case in this route — same carve-out justification as M3).
- **Engine wiring**: route never touches `cost_layers.qty_remaining`, `cost_layer_consumptions.*`, `movement.total_cost`, or `item.current_qty`. Increase: `record_receipt` is the single owner. Decrease: `consume_fifo` is the single owner. Caller pattern is identical to M2 / M3.
- **Audit shape**: `action="stock_movement.adjustment"`, `entity_type="stock_movement"`, `entity_id=movement.id`, `before=None`, `after`:
  - **Increase**: `{item_id, qty, direction="increase", unit_cost, total_cost, source="positive_adjustment", reason, note, received_at}`. Decimal scale on `total_cost` is the input scale (e.g. `"12.50"` for `5 × 2.50`) because `record_receipt` computes the product in memory before the column round-trip.
  - **Decrease**: `{item_id, qty, direction, total_cost, reason, note}`. **No `unit_cost` / `source` / `received_at`** (varies per layer; matches M3's stock-out audit shape). `total_cost` carries the column-quantised scale 4 (e.g. `"8.0000"`) because the engine reads `layer.unit_cost` back from `Numeric(14,4)` storage — same wart as M3's stock-out audit.
- **`unit_cost` field is rendered for both directions** but only parsed + required for increase. For decrease, garbage in the field is accepted (and ignored). The form's `<em>required for increases; ignored for decreases</em>` hint is the user-facing cue. Conservative: doesn't need HTMX swap (still no concrete second use case for HTMX).
- **Templates**: new `stock_adjust_form.html` mirroring `stock_out_form.html` with the addition of a `direction` `<select>` (`stock-adjust-direction-input` test-id; both `increase` and `decrease` options) and the always-rendered `unit_cost` input. Reason input is HTML-required + `*`-marked. Test-ids: `stock-adjust-form`, `stock-adjust-qty-input`, `stock-adjust-direction-input`, `stock-adjust-unit-cost-input`, `stock-adjust-reason-input`, `stock-adjust-note-input`, `stock-adjust-submit`, `stock-adjust-error`. `items_form.html` gains a third `data-testid="stock-adjust-link"` "Adjust →" link in the same `{% if not item.archived_at %}` block as in / out.
- **Test coverage** (`tests/integration/test_movements_routes.py` 45 new + `tests/e2e/test_movements_e2e.py` extension):
  - Role enforcement (10): anon GET / POST 401; pending 403; Workshop / Office / Manager / Admin all 200 GET / 303 POST. Increase POST tests don't need a seed; decrease POST tests in this matrix go through the increase path so a layer isn't needed.
  - Form rendering (5): inputs + CSRF + both directions + reason marked required; current_qty + open_value surfaced; recent-movements empty state; unknown 404; archived 400.
  - Validation matrix (16): qty blank / zero / negative / non-numeric (4); direction blank / invalid (2); reason blank / whitespace-only (2); unit_cost on increase blank / negative / non-numeric (3); zero unit_cost on increase allowed (1); unit_cost ignored on decrease (1); unknown 404 + archived 400 on POST (2); failed validation writes no audit (1).
  - Increase happy path (4): creates `StockMovement(type=ADJUSTMENT)` + `CostLayer(source=POSITIVE_ADJUSTMENT)` + bumps current_qty; total_cost = qty × unit_cost (e.g. `60.00`); audit content with `direction=increase`, `unit_cost`, `source`, `received_at` present; whitespace strip on reason / note; flash includes `+qty`.
  - Decrease happy path (4): creates `StockMovement(type=ADJUSTMENT)` + `CostLayerConsumption` rows + decrements current_qty; total_cost is layer-weighted; audit content with `direction=decrease`, no unit_cost / source / received_at; blank-note-becomes-None; flash includes `-qty`.
  - Insufficient stock on decrease (3): atomic rollback (no movement / consumption / qty mutation; layer.qty_remaining unchanged); in-form error block + preserved inputs (incl. direction value); no audit on insufficient stock.
  - Multi-layer FIFO on decrease (1): two layers (4 @ 2.00 + 6 @ 3.00, distinct received_at), decrease 7 → consumes 4 from old + 3 from new; total_cost = 4×2 + 3×3 = 17.00; consumption rows ordered correctly; current_qty = 3.
  - Adjust link on edit form (2): visible for active item; hidden for archived.
  - E2E walk extension: after the existing OUT + insufficient-stock legs (current_qty=70 at that point), workshop deep-links to `/admin/items/{id}/adjust`. Leg 1 (increase): qty=20, unit_cost=3.00, reason="found extra" → flash with `+20`, current_qty=90, recent-movements row with reason + 20 + 60. Leg 2 (decrease): qty=15, reason="damaged batch" → flash with `-15`, current_qty=75, recent-movements row.

**Manual stock-out route (M3):** `app/movements.py` gains two more routes mounted under `/admin/items` for **Manager + Office + Workshop**: `GET /admin/items/{item_id}/out` renders a form (qty + reason + note — *no* unit_cost; consumption price is per-layer, not per-movement) plus the existing recent-movements table and a new "open value" summary line (sum across the item's open FIFO layers, computed via `open_value`); `POST /admin/items/{item_id}/out` validates, builds a `StockMovement(type=OUT)`, flushes for an id, calls `consume_fifo(db, item=..., qty=..., movement=...)`, writes a `stock_movement.out` audit row, commits, 303s back with a flash. The handler-level body mirrors `record_stock_in` line-for-line (different engine call + audit action + redirect), so the helper set introduced by M2 (`_parse_positive_decimal`, `_get_item_or_404`, `_reject_archived`, `_flash`, `_recent_movements`) is reused as-is. One new helper: `_render_stock_out_form` factors the GET-and-error rendering paths so the insufficient-stock 400 path doesn't fork.

- **Insufficient-stock path (the new shape choice in M3):** the engine raises `InsufficientStockError(item_id, requested, available)` *before* any mutation (atomic-on-raise tested in M1). The route catches the error, calls `db.rollback()` (drops the unflushed `StockMovement` we added before the engine call — the engine itself never mutated anything, so the rollback's only job is to discard the orphan movement row), reloads the item via `_get_item_or_404` (because the rolled-back transaction left the original `item` reference detached), and re-renders the form via `_render_stock_out_form` with HTTP 400, the user's qty / reason / note preserved in the inputs, and an `<p data-testid="stock-out-error" role="alert">` block carrying the message "Not enough stock: requested {N}, only {M} available." This is the **only** form in the app today that re-renders on validation 400 — every other settings form (suppliers / locations / taxonomy / field-defs / items / item-units / stock-in) lets a 400 land on FastAPI's bare exception page. The carve-out is justified because insufficient-stock is a *data-dependent* failure (changes minute-by-minute as other actors consume) where typing the form again is more friction than re-typing a typo. The other validation 400s (blank qty, negative qty, archived item, etc.) follow the existing convention — bare 400 — so this is one carve-out, not a new pattern. Self-critique flags the inconsistency for a future "in-form errors" sweep across all seven forms.
- **Engine wiring**: route never touches `cost_layers.qty_remaining`, `cost_layer_consumptions.*`, `movement.total_cost`, or `item.current_qty` — those are M1's invariants and `consume_fifo` is the single owner. Caller pattern is the same as M2: `db.add(movement); db.flush(); consume_fifo(...); record_audit(...); db.commit()`. The route does not surface a backdated `created_at` UI in M3 — same gap as M2.
- **Audit shape**: `action="stock_movement.out"`, `entity_type="stock_movement"`, `entity_id=movement.id`, `before=None`, `after={item_id, qty, total_cost, reason, note}`. **No `unit_cost`** (varies per layer — the layer-weighted sum is captured in `total_cost`). **No `source`** (consumes don't carry one). The layer-level breakdown is queryable from `cost_layer_consumptions WHERE movement_id = ?` — also append-only-by-engine per M1's contract — so duplicating it in the audit row would re-encode information already durably stored. Decimals are stringified via `str(decimal)` to preserve the column-quantised representation through JSON (the engine reads `layer.unit_cost` back from `Numeric(14,4)`, so `total_cost = qty * unit_cost` carries scale 4 — see the test for `total_cost == "8.0000"` not `"8"`).
- **Templates**: new `stock_out_form.html` — same shape as `stock_in_form.html` but without the unit_cost input, with an "Open value" summary line (`data-testid="item-open-value"`), and with an `{% if error %}<p data-testid="stock-out-error" role="alert">` block above the form for the insufficient-stock case. Test-ids: `stock-out-form` / `stock-out-qty-input` / `stock-out-reason-input` / `stock-out-note-input` / `stock-out-submit` / `stock-out-error`. `items_form.html` gains a `data-testid="stock-out-link"` "Stock out →" link alongside the existing "Stock in →" link, on the same conditions (item not archived; visible to whoever can see the edit form — Manager + Office today).
- **Test coverage** (`tests/integration/test_movements_routes.py` 37 new + `tests/e2e/test_movements_e2e.py` extension = 37 integration + 1 e2e leg-pair):
  - Role enforcement (10): anonymous GET / POST 401, pending 403, Workshop / Office / Manager / Admin all succeed (200 GET / 303 POST). Role POST tests seed a layer first via `_seed_layer` (a tiny helper that goes through `record_receipt` so the seed itself exercises the receipt path).
  - Form rendering (7): inputs + CSRF present; no `name="unit_cost"` in the body; current_qty + open_value surfaced; open_value=0 for an item with no layers; recent-movements empty state; recent-movements populated after a seed; unknown item 404; archived item 400.
  - Validation (7): blank / zero / negative / non-numeric qty 400; unknown item 404 on POST; archived item 400 on POST; failed validation writes no audit row.
  - Happy path (5): single-layer consume creates `StockMovement(type=OUT)` with the right total_cost (3 × 2.50 = 7.50 for the headline assertion), one `CostLayerConsumption` row pointing at the right layer / movement / qty / unit_cost_at_consumption, decremented `layer.qty_remaining`, decremented `item.current_qty`; whitespace strip on reason + note; blank reason + note → None; audit row keys + values (incl. `total_cost == "8.0000"`, no `unit_cost`, no `source`); flash includes item name.
  - Insufficient stock (4): consume more than open layers → 400 + form re-rendered + error block + qty / reason / note preserved + no movement / consumption / current_qty / qty_remaining mutation; consume from item with no layers at all → 400 + error block; no audit row written on insufficient stock; consume *exactly* the open balance succeeds (303, layer drained to qty_remaining=0 but kept).
  - Multi-layer FIFO (2): two layers with distinct received_at → consume 7 of (4, 6) takes 4 from old + 3 from new; total_cost = 4×2.00 + 3×3.00 = 17.00; old layer drained, new partially consumed; consumption rows ordered correctly. Recent-movements list correctly shows both the seed IN and the new OUT for the same item.
  - Stock-out link (2): edit form shows the "Stock out →" link for an active item; hides it for an archived item.
  - E2E walk extension: after the existing stock-in step, workshop deep-links to `/admin/items/{id}/out`, asserts current_qty=100.0000 + open_value contains "250", fills qty=30 / reason="Production run", submits; flash, bumped current_qty=70.0000, OUT row showing "Production run" + 30 + 75 (total_cost = 30 × 2.50). Then a second leg: fills qty=1000, submits, asserts the `stock-out-error` block contains "Not enough stock", inputs preserved, current_qty unchanged at 70.0000.

**Manual stock-in route (M2):** `app/movements.py` exposes two routes mounted under `/admin/items` for **Manager + Office + Workshop**: `GET /admin/items/{item_id}/in` renders a form (qty + unit_cost + reason + note) plus a recent-movements table (last 10, newest first); `POST /admin/items/{item_id}/in` validates, builds a `StockMovement(type=IN)`, flushes for an id, calls `record_receipt(...)` with `source=MANUAL_IN`, writes a `stock_movement.in` audit row, commits, and 303s back to the same form with a flash. Workshop's first positive-write surface — CSRF + role gating both server-enforced.

- **Validation** (all 400, *before* any DB write so failures are atomic): `qty` parses as a strictly-positive `Decimal` (blank, zero, negative, non-numeric all reject); `unit_cost` parses as a non-negative `Decimal` (blank, negative, non-numeric reject; zero allowed for sample/gifted stock); `reason` and `note` stripped, blank → `None`. Item must exist (404) and not be archived (400 — same posture as taxonomy/items "no new structure under archived").
- **Engine wiring**: route never touches `cost_layers.qty_remaining`, `movement.total_cost`, or `item.current_qty` — those are M1's invariants and `record_receipt` is the single owner. Caller pattern is exactly what M1 documented: `db.add(movement); db.flush(); record_receipt(db, ..., movement=movement); record_audit(...); db.commit()`. The route does *not* set `received_at` to anything other than `now()` in M2 — backdated UI is deferred to PO5/M4 even though the engine supports it.
- **Audit shape**: `action="stock_movement.in"`, `entity_type="stock_movement"`, `entity_id=movement.id`, `before=None`, `after={item_id, qty, unit_cost, total_cost, source, reason, note, received_at}`. Decimals are stringified via `str(decimal)` to preserve precision through JSON (same convention as I2's custom-field audit shape). The cost layer and any future consumption rows are reconstructable from `cost_layers.source_movement_id` and `cost_layer_consumptions.movement_id`.
- **Templates**: new `stock_in_form.html` (page-shaped, not HTMX-partial — HTMX swap deferred until a second use case exists). Renders the form + a `data-testid="movements-table"` with one `data-testid="movement-row"` per recent movement (columns: when / type / qty / total_cost / actor / reason). Empty-state `data-testid="movements-empty"` when no movements yet. `items_form.html` gains a `data-testid="stock-in-link"` "Stock in →" link visible to the edit form's audience (Manager + Office) when the item is not archived.
- **Test coverage** (`tests/integration/test_movements_routes.py` 38 + `tests/e2e/test_movements_e2e.py` 1 = 39 new):
  - Role enforcement (10): anonymous GET 401, anonymous POST 401, pending 403, every active role (Workshop, Office, Manager, Admin) succeeds on GET 200 and POST 303.
  - Form rendering (6): inputs + CSRF present; current_qty surfaced; recent-movements empty state; recent-movements list populated (asserts row count via `data-testid="movement-row"`); unknown item 404; archived item 400.
  - Validation matrix (12): blank/zero/negative/non-numeric qty 400; blank/negative/non-numeric unit_cost 400; zero unit_cost allowed; unknown item 404 on POST; archived item 400 on POST; failed validation writes no audit row.
  - Happy path (6): single receipt creates movement (with type=IN, item_id, qty, user_id, reason, note, total_cost, po_id=None, stock_take_id=None) + cost layer (with qty_received=qty_remaining=qty, unit_cost, source=MANUAL_IN, source_movement_id=movement.id) + bumps item.current_qty; whitespace-strip on reason + note; blank reason + note → None; audit row keys + values; flash message after redirect; decimal precision preserved on qty + unit_cost.
  - Multi-receipt (3): two consecutive receipts create two layers with the right unit_costs + accumulate qty; recent-movements newest-first ordering; sibling items don't show each other's movements.
  - Stock-in link (2): edit form shows the "Stock in →" link for an active item; hides it for an archived item.
  - E2E walk (1): pending workshop user is admin-promoted; pending manager user is admin-promoted (admin signs in twice — once per promotion since role + status are two POSTs); manager creates a category + item; workshop deep-links to `/admin/items/{id}/in`, asserts the empty-movements state + zero current_qty, fills qty=100 / unit_cost=2.50 / reason="First receipt", submits, asserts the flash + bumped current_qty=100.0000 + the new movement row showing the reason + qty + total_cost (250). Cleanup archives the item + the category.

**FIFO cost engine (M1):** `app/cost_engine.py` exposes three pure functions and one exception. The engine is the single owner of `item.current_qty`, `cost_layers.qty_remaining`, and `stock_movements.total_cost` going forward — every M2-M6 / PO5 / ST-series route must call into it rather than touching those columns directly.

- `record_receipt(db, *, item, qty, unit_cost, source, movement, received_at=None) -> CostLayer` — creates a layer with `qty_received=qty_remaining=qty`, increments `item.current_qty`, sets `movement.total_cost = qty * unit_cost`. Validates `qty > 0`, `unit_cost >= 0` (zero allowed for sample/gifted stock), and that `movement.id` is set (caller must `db.flush()` first).
- `consume_fifo(db, *, item, qty, movement) -> Decimal` — walks open layers in `(received_at ASC, id ASC)` order, creates one `CostLayerConsumption` per layer touched, decrements `qty_remaining`, accumulates total cost, decrements `item.current_qty`, sets `movement.total_cost`. Atomic — raises `InsufficientStockError(item_id, requested, available)` *before any mutation* if open layers don't sum to `qty`. Validates `qty > 0` and flushed movement.
- `open_value(db, item) -> Decimal` — read-only sum of `qty_remaining * unit_cost` across the item's layers with `qty_remaining > 0`. Returns `Decimal("0")` for an item with no open layers.

**Schema (migration `0010_create_cost_layers_and_movements.py`):** three new tables, in dependency order (`stock_movements` first so the cost tables can FK into it).

- `stock_movements`: `id, item_id (FK RESTRICT, NOT NULL), item_unit_id (FK RESTRICT nullable), type (String(16), SAEnum-backed: in/out/adjustment/transfer), qty (Numeric(14,4)), user_id (FK SET NULL nullable), reason (String(255) nullable), note (String(2000) nullable), po_id (Integer nullable, NO FK in M1), stock_take_id (Integer nullable, NO FK in M1), total_cost (Numeric(14,4) nullable — engine sets it), created_at`. Five indexes: per-item, per-item_unit, per-user, per-type, per-created_at. `po_id` and `stock_take_id` are plain integers (no FK) because the `purchase_orders` and `stock_takes` tables don't exist yet — the FK constraint is added in PO2 / ST1's migration.
- `cost_layers`: `id, item_id (FK RESTRICT, NOT NULL), qty_received (Numeric(14,4) NOT NULL — immutable post-insert), qty_remaining (Numeric(14,4) NOT NULL — only the engine decrements this), unit_cost (Numeric(14,4) NOT NULL — immutable), received_at (DateTime(tz) NOT NULL — caller-supplied or now()), source (String(20), SAEnum-backed: po_receipt/manual_in/positive_adjustment), source_movement_id (FK stock_movements.id RESTRICT NOT NULL), created_at`. Three indexes: per-item, per-source_movement, plus the composite `ix_cost_layers_item_received` on `(item_id, received_at, id)` that covers the FIFO ORDER BY.
- `cost_layer_consumptions`: `id, layer_id (FK RESTRICT NOT NULL), movement_id (FK RESTRICT NOT NULL), qty_consumed (Numeric(14,4) NOT NULL), unit_cost_at_consumption (Numeric(14,4) NOT NULL — snapshot of the layer's unit_cost at the time of the consume), created_at`. Three indexes: per-layer, per-movement, plus a composite `ix_cost_layer_consumptions_movement_layer` so an item-detail page (M6) can fetch a movement's full breakdown in one query.

No `archived_at` on any of the three. The engine maintains six invariants (documented in `app/cost_engine.py`'s module docstring): receipts only INSERT layers and INCREMENT qty; consumes only INSERT consumptions, DECREMENT `qty_remaining`, and DECREMENT `current_qty`; `qty_received` / `unit_cost` / `received_at` / `source` are immutable; nothing is ever DELETEd; `movement.total_cost` is set exactly once per engine call; FIFO order is `(received_at ASC, id ASC)`.

**Two new enums** in `app/models.py`: `MovementType(IN, OUT, ADJUSTMENT, TRANSFER)` and `CostLayerSource(PO_RECEIPT, MANUAL_IN, POSITIVE_ADJUSTMENT)`. Both stored as `String(16)` / `String(20)` via SAEnum + `values_callable`, matching the existing `Role` / `UserStatus` / `TrackingMode` / `ItemUnitStatus` / `FieldType` convention.

**Test coverage** (`tests/unit/test_cost_models.py` 15 tests + `tests/unit/test_cost_engine.py` 29 tests = 44 new):

- Models (15): minimal-defaults round-trip per table, every enum value round-trips, FK NOT NULL violations raise IntegrityError, `qty_remaining` decrement does not affect `qty_received`, `po_id`/`stock_take_id` accept arbitrary integers (no FK constraint), `total_cost` round-trips Numeric(14,4), two consumptions can share a movement (multi-layer consume case).
- Engine — receipt (9): correct layer fields, `current_qty` increment, `movement.total_cost` set, `received_at=None` defaults to now (within ±1s), explicit `received_at` honoured, `qty <= 0` raises ValueError, negative `unit_cost` raises, zero `unit_cost` allowed, unflushed movement raises ValueError.
- Engine — consume single-layer (2): partial consume creates one consumption row + decrements layer + sets total_cost; exact consume drains layer to 0 (layer kept, not deleted).
- Engine — consume multi-layer (3): two layers spanned in FIFO order with mixed unit costs, exhausted layer skipped (no consumption row written for it), id-tiebreak when received_at is identical (uses `freezegun` to force the timestamp tie).
- Engine — errors (6): `InsufficientStockError` carries `item_id`/`requested`/`available`; over-consume is atomic (no layers / qty / consumption rows mutated, `total_cost` stays None); empty-layer-set raises; zero qty raises; negative qty raises; unflushed movement raises.
- Engine — isolation (1): item A's layers are not consumed when item B's consume runs (and fails).
- Engine — `open_value` (6): empty returns 0, single layer, multi-layer sum across mixed sources, exhausted layer excluded, partial layer included, isolation between items.
- Engine — combined (2): full receipt → consume → receipt → consume cycle verifies the running `current_qty` net + `open_value` after each step; positive adjustment → negative adjustment cycle exercises the same paths through the adjustment movement type.

**What's running (route surface unchanged from I3a):** **Manager + Admin** can fully manage items via `/admin/items` (including custom field values inherited from the leaf node's schema) and per-unit rows for unique-tracked items via `/admin/items/{id}/units`. **Office** can list + edit items + units (cannot create/archive either, cannot change reorder thresholds — MISSION §3). **Workshop** still 403s on every items / units endpoint (read-only access deferred). 14 URL patterns total (7 items + 7 units, all CSRF-protected). M1 is pre-route — the cost engine is callable but no HTTP handler invokes it yet; that's M2's job. Items routes:

- `GET  /admin/items?[show=active|archived&node_id=N]` — Manager + Office. List with active/archived tabs, optional filter by taxonomy node.
- `GET  /admin/items/new[?node_id=N]` — Manager-only. Form, pre-selects category from query string when supplied.
- `POST /admin/items` — Manager-only. Create.
- `GET  /admin/items/{item_id}/edit` — Manager + Office. Form, with archived-FK preservation (see below).
- `POST /admin/items/{item_id}` — Manager + Office. Update (sparse audit diff). Office's threshold submissions are silently overridden with the existing row's values *before* validation, so no audit diff for Office can ever include `reorder_threshold` / `reorder_qty`.
- `POST /admin/items/{item_id}/archive` + `/unarchive` — Manager-only. Idempotent; no audit row on no-op.

**Unit routes** (I3, all under `/admin/items/...` but in a separate router module `app/item_units.py`):

- `GET  /admin/items/{item_id}/units?[show=active|archived]` — Manager + Office. List per-item units; renders a "qty-tracked" note + hidden CTA when the parent item is qty-tracked, an "archived" note when the parent is archived.
- `GET  /admin/items/{item_id}/units/new` — Manager-only. Form. 400 if item is qty-tracked or archived (no new structure under archived parents — same posture as taxonomy sub-cats / field defs).
- `POST /admin/items/{item_id}/units` — Manager-only. Create. Same archived-parent + qty-tracked guards.
- `GET  /admin/items/units/{unit_id}/edit` — Manager + Office. Flat-by-id form (parent in URL would just confuse callers; unit's `item_id` is the source of truth).
- `POST /admin/items/units/{unit_id}` — Manager + Office. Update (sparse audit diff: only changed fields appear in `before/after_json`).
- `POST /admin/items/units/{unit_id}/{archive,unarchive}` — Manager-only. Idempotent. **Archiving a unit under an archived parent item is allowed** (cleanup workflow, mirrors S4's archived-parent stance).

**Threshold gating** (MISSION §3 "Office cannot change reorder thresholds"): handled in `_can_edit_thresholds(user) -> bool`, which returns True for Manager + Admin only. Used in both `update_item` (overrides inbound form values for Office) and `edit_item_form` (drives the template's `can_edit_thresholds` flag → hides inputs, shows read-only display values mirroring the `current_qty` pattern). Silent override (rather than 400) was chosen for consistency with `current_qty` and because it's how an HTML form's hidden field would behave for a non-tampered client.

**Archived-FK preservation**: `_resolve_optional_supplier`, `_resolve_optional_location`, `_resolve_leaf_node` each take a `current_id` kwarg. Contract: blank → None (clears the link, even if the previous value was archived — explicit user choice); a non-blank archived id is accepted *only if* it matches `current_id`; switching to a *different* archived id still 400s. The form-side helpers `_supplier_options`, `_location_options`, `_leaf_options` likewise take `current_id` and append the assigned-but-archived row to the dropdown with an "(archived)" suffix (and for sub-cat leaves, "Parent / Sub (archived)"). Archived rows that aren't the current assignment are *not* listed — the dropdown doesn't become a graveyard; only the active set + the row the item is pinned to.

**Leaf invariant** (reused from S5): a top-level node with no active sub-categories is a leaf; a sub-category is always a leaf. `_is_leaf(db, node)` is duplicated between `app/items.py` and `app/field_defs.py` — two callers, one-line predicate, both must move in lockstep if the leaf rule changes. Acceptable today; flagged for extraction once a third caller arrives.

**Validations** (all return 400 on failure unless noted):
- `sku` / `name` / `unit` non-empty after strip; `sku` unique across active+archived rows (same convention as Supplier names).
- `taxonomy_node_id` must reference an existing, non-archived leaf node — non-leaf still 400; archived rejected *unless* it matches the row's existing `taxonomy_node_id` (preserve-unchanged contract).
- `tracking_mode` parses to `TrackingMode` enum (`qty`, `unique`).
- `reorder_threshold` / `reorder_qty` parse as non-negative `Decimal`; blank → 0. Office's submissions are silently overridden with the existing values before this parser runs (so Office can't even fail validation on these fields).
- Optional `supplier_id` / `location_id`: blank → None (clears even if the previous was archived — explicit user action); if set, must reference an active row *or* match the existing assignment if archived.
- `qr_code` blank → None; otherwise unique across all rows where set (partial unique index).
- `current_qty` is **not** writable through the route — pinned at 0 on create; preserved unchanged on edit. Stock movements (M1+) own this column.

**Audit vocabulary**: `item.created`, `item.updated`, `item.archived`, `item.unarchived`. Created `after_json` carries the full set of stored fields (incl. current_qty for completeness) plus a `custom_fields` dict (key → audit-friendly value) when any custom values were set. Updates use the `_diff` sparse-changed-fields pattern; custom-field changes appear under a `custom_fields` sub-dict that *only* contains keys whose value changed (sparse: `before["custom_fields"]["alloy"] = "silver"` / `after["custom_fields"]["alloy"] = "gold"`, with no entries for unchanged fields). Office actors *cannot* produce a diff that includes `reorder_threshold` / `reorder_qty` (those are inert before the diff runs).

**Custom field values (I2)**: items inherit the **active** field defs of their leaf node. Values are stored sparsely in `item_field_values` (one row per `(item_id, field_def_id)` with a non-null value; the column is chosen by the def's type — `value_text` / `value_number` / `value_decimal` / `value_date` / `value_bool` / `value_json` for multiselect, with select also using `value_text` for the chosen option). Boolean rows persist both `True` and `False` (a checkbox always has a definite answer); every other type skips the row when the parsed value is blank/empty. Required-flag enforcement: text/number/decimal/date/select/multiselect must be non-blank/non-empty; **boolean must be `True`** (an unchecked required boolean = "must confirm" pattern, not a missing answer — documented in `app/items.py`'s module docstring). Audit values: decimals → str (preserves precision), dates → ISO, lists pass through, primitives pass through. Archived field defs are intentionally invisible to the form — existing values stay on the item ("Deleting a field hides it from new entry but preserves the value in audit history", MISSION §3); the diff-and-apply path only iterates *active* defs, so archived rows never get touched. Required-flag, type-coercion, and out-of-options select / multiselect violations all `raise HTTPException(400)` and short-circuit before any item write — atomic.

**Migration:** `migrations/versions/0008_create_item_field_values.py` adds the `item_field_values` table + 3 indexes (`uq_item_field_values_item_field_def` UNIQUE on `(item_id, field_def_id)`; `ix_item_field_values_item_id`; `ix_item_field_values_field_def_id`). The unique index makes the "one row per (item, field def)" invariant a storage-layer guarantee, not just a route convention.

**Templates (I2 updates):**
- `items_form.html` — Adds a `{% if field_defs %}` fieldset after the core fields. One `<input>`/`<select>`/`<textarea>` per active def, dispatched by type: text → text input; number → `<input type="number">`; decimal → text+`inputmode="decimal"`; date → `<input type="date">`; boolean → checkbox; select → `<select>` with `— pick one —` blank option; multiselect → `<select multiple>`. Form names are `cf_<key>`; pre-fill from `form.custom[key]`. Required marker is the same `<span aria-hidden="true">*</span>` pattern as the core fields. Test-ids: `item-cf-<key>-input` per input + `item-custom-fields` on the fieldset + `item-cf-row` per row (with `data-cf-key="<key>"`).
- (I1b updates carried forward unchanged: `items_list.html` and `base.html` role gates.)

**Known broken:** none. **Resolved warts:**
- ~~Archived-FK silent data loss on item edit~~ (I1a → I1b)
- ~~Items don't inherit field schema~~ (S5 → I2)

---

## Current slice

*(none — slice C3 just shipped, see Completed log)*

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — C3:**

- **No DB-level uniqueness on the open-checkout invariant** (carried forward from C2). C3 didn't introduce a new race surface, but the existing one is more visible now: two operators clicking "Check in" on the same open row simultaneously would both pass the `returned_at IS NULL` guard, then both `UPDATE` the row. The second write wins for `condition_note` (last note overrides) and `returned_at` (later timestamp wins by 1ms). The audit log gets two `checkout.returned` rows. Not destructive — the row is closed either way — but the audit log will show two distinct returns, which would confuse a reader. Same fix shape as C2's: a partial unique index `(item_id, item_unit_id) WHERE returned_at IS NULL`. Out of scope for v1 at workshop scale; flagged for the same P-series tightening pass as C2.
- **Cross-actor returns by design.** A workshop user can return a manager's checkout. Audit row's `actor_id` records the returner; the borrower (`user_id` on the checkout row) is preserved. Pinned by `test_workshop_can_return_other_users_checkout`. MISSION §3 is silent on a borrower-only rule; the workshop reality is that whoever's at the bench returns the tool. If real users want a "borrower only" or "manager-can-override" toggle, the change is one line in the route + one new test.
- **Note merging is overwrite-with-history-via-separator**, not a separate `condition_note_at_return` column. Trade-off: a future "search returns where the note contains X" requires substring search (the C2 + C3 notes are concatenated). The alternative (a second column) would mean a migration + an audit-shape change + form template branching for "is this the C2 or C3 note?". The single-column-with-separator approach keeps the model thin and the audit shape unchanged. Documented.
- **Merged-note overflow is a hard 400, not a "truncate the existing"**. If a long-existing + long-fresh exceeds 2000 chars, the route rejects rather than dropping characters from the existing note. The user has to shorten the fresh note. Conservative: silent truncation would lose audit-relevant context. The 400 message names the field; the error page is FastAPI's default. Flagged: a friendlier in-form error (the same carve-out as M3's stock-out error) would let the user see the merged size before submit.
- **No "are you sure" prompt before check-in.** A misclick closes the checkout. The audit log preserves the action, and a new `Checkout` row could be created (re-checkout) but the original is closed. Conservative: no JS confirm in v1; same posture as PO5's receive button and PO2b's cancel button. Could add a `<details>` "danger zone"-style wrapper around the submit if real users complain.
- **Status block is per-item, not global.** A manager browsing the items list still doesn't see "currently out / overdue" — that's C4's job. C3 only wires the same-page workflow (operator who just looked at this item's status block can also return from there). Documented; C4 is the next slice.
- **`<details>` element relies on browser native rendering.** No JS, no Tailwind required — `<details>`/`<summary>` is a Web Standard widely supported since 2019 in all major browsers (Chrome, Firefox, Safari, Edge). On a workshop tablet running modern Chrome (the v1 target per MISSION §4), it works out of the box. If we ever target an ancient embedded browser, fallback would be a custom `<button>` that toggles a hidden div via inline `onclick`. Acceptable.
- **Audit `before` field is a partial diff** (`returned_at`+`condition_note`) not the full prior `Checkout` row. Consistent with M3 / M4 / PO2b audit shapes (only changed fields appear in `before` / `after`). A reader who wants the full prior state can join back to the `Checkout` row by `entity_id`.
- **No `expected_return` re-rendering on the return record.** A checkout returned 3 days late doesn't get a "this was overdue" flag on the `checkout.returned` audit row. Reporting can derive overdue-ness by comparing `returned_at` to `expected_return` from the Checkout row (or, for currently-out checkouts, comparing now() to expected_return). C4's manager view will surface this; the audit row is intentionally minimal.
- **No partial returns for qty-tracked checkouts.** A qty-tracked checkout in v1 is binary (out / in). MISSION §3 ("check out a tool or mould") frames this as unit-level; partial returns for a "borrowed 5 / returned 3" scenario would need a `qty_returned` column + an updated state model. Out of scope for v1.
- **Test coverage uses `_open_checkout` helper that bypasses the C2 route** — sets `Checkout.checked_out_at` to a fixed `datetime(2026, 5, 1, 9, 0, UTC)` so the tests don't depend on the C2 POST being green. Trade-off: a future C2 contract change (e.g. the audit shape) wouldn't be caught by these tests. Acceptable: the C2 audit shape has its own dedicated tests (`TestCheckoutQtyHappyPath` / `TestCheckoutUniqueHappyPath`); these C3 tests target the C3 contract.

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — C2:**

- **No DB-level uniqueness on the open-checkout invariant.** A partial unique index `(item_id, item_unit_id) WHERE returned_at IS NULL` would catch the race where two simultaneous POSTs read no-open-checkout and both insert. Today the route layer is the sole guard. Same posture as the rest of the codebase (taxonomy leaf invariants, item-units qty-vs-unique rule). Flagged for a future P-series tightening pass — at v1 scale (a workshop with one or two staff scanning at a time) the race is vanishingly rare.
- **Workshop self-checkout only.** There's no "check this out on behalf of $other_user" UI. A workshop user can only check things out *to themselves*; the route reads `user.id` from the session. MISSION §3 doesn't require the on-behalf-of variant; if it ever does, add a `for_user_id` param to the POST gated on `Manager` role and the audit row's `user_id` carries the assignee while the actor (`actor_id`) records who hit submit. Documented for C-series follow-up.
- **`expected_return` is a date, not a datetime.** The `<input type="date">` produces YYYY-MM-DD; the route upgrades to UTC midnight for the column. A real workshop's "due back at 5pm Friday" can't be expressed today. Out of scope for v1; the workflow is "due by end of day on date X" and overdue-by-time-of-day is a polish concern.
- **No pre-fill of `expected_return` from a default offset.** A polish pass could pre-fill it with `today + 7 days` (or per-item config) so the operator doesn't have to type a date for the common case. Out of scope for v1.
- **The status block is read-only — no per-row "check this back in" button.** That belongs to C3. C2's status block exists to surface "this is already out" as a *confirmation* signal, not an action surface. C3 will add a check-in form (probably a small POST per row from the same page) and the status block becomes the entry point.
- **No "checked out" label on the items list.** A manager browsing the items list can't see at a glance which flagged items are currently out. That's C4's job (manager "currently out / overdue" view). The items list stays focused on "what stock do we own"; the checkout state is a secondary read.
- **Non-flagged item GET → 400.** A workshop user who deep-links to `/admin/items/{id}/checkout` for a non-flagged item gets a bare 400 page. The friendlier UX is to redirect to the item's detail with a flash explaining why. Conservative: 400 matches every other validation 400 in the codebase outside M3 / M4's data-dependent stock-shortage carve-out. The link is gated on `requires_checkout=True` in both `items_form.html` and `item_detail.html`, so a real user only hits the 400 via a stale link or manual URL editing.
- **The qty-tracked "already checked out" guard rejects new POSTs but the GET form still renders + accepts a submit.** The GET shows `checkout-no-submit-note` when there's no path forward, but the POST path validates regardless. A user with a stale form could still submit and get a 400. The bare 400 is the right posture; the GET's "no submit" rendering is the friendly affordance for the common case. Not a bug — same posture as the unique-tracked "no available units" case.
- **Post-create redirect targets the same `/checkout` URL** rather than `/detail` or the items list. After a successful checkout, the user lands back on the form with the just-checked-out unit visible in the status block + removed from the available select — confirming the action visually. The trade-off is a manager doing many checkouts in a row stays on the same item's page; for "check out a different tool" they navigate via the items list. Acceptable; same redirect-to-form pattern as M2 / M3 / M4 / M5 / PO5.
- **The `audit_log` `entity_type="checkout"` is a new entity type.** Prior types: user, supplier, location, taxonomy_node, taxonomy_field_def, item, item_unit, stock_movement, purchase_order. C2's `checkout` slots in cleanly. C3 will add `checkout.returned`; C4 will not write new audit rows (read-only manager view). Pinned by the integration test's `_audit_rows(db, action="checkout.created")` filter.
- **No "checkout history" view per item.** A manager can't see "who has had this tool over the past month" without querying the audit log directly. C4's manager view will surface currently-out + overdue; a "history" view is a polish concern that may belong to the R-series (alongside the audit-log report).

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — C1:**

- **Filter is 2-state (all / requires checkout), not 3-state.** A user might expect "show only items that DON'T require checkout". Today `?requires_checkout=no` falls through to no filter — same as blank or any other value. v1 enumerates only the on/off case ("which items are tools / moulds?") because the inverse query has no DoD #4 use case. If real users ask, the change is one line in the route + one new nav link.
- **`Checkout?` column adds noise on shops with no flagged items.** Could conditionally render the column only when at least one row is flagged. Not worth the per-page branching; the "—" cell is small and stable.
- **No DB-level constraint on the route invariants** — open-checkout uniqueness, qty-tracked-vs-unique-tracked rule, `requires_checkout=True` precondition. Those land in the route layer (C2 onward) per the same posture as taxonomy leaf invariants and item-units qty-tracked invariants. A partial unique index on `(item_id) WHERE returned_at IS NULL AND item_unit_id IS NULL` (and a sibling for unit-tracked) would catch races that the route layer can't. Out of scope for v1; flagged for a P-series tightening pass once C2-C4 land.
- **`ix_checkouts_returned_at` is a B-tree, not partial-on-NULL.** Postgres handles NULL fine; SQLite too. Partial-on-NULL would be tighter but adds backend branching for marginal gain at v1 scale (tens of open checkouts at a time). Acceptable.
- **No e2e walk in this slice** — schema-only + UI affordance. C2's check-out flow is the right place to add the walk (creates a checkout row, asserts the table accepts the write, exercises the `returned_at IS NULL` derivation). Adding a walk now would just verify the column shows "Yes" for a manager-flagged item, which the integration suite already covers.
- **`Checkout` model docstring documents the C2 invariants ("at most one open checkout per item / item_unit", "unique-tracked items require item_unit_id") that are not yet enforced by the route or DB.** That's intentional — the docstring is a forward-looking contract for C2 — but a reader of `models.py` today would see invariants that aren't enforced anywhere. Acceptable: the contract is honest about the "C-series enforces this", and grepping `app/` for `Checkout` from C2 onward will find the enforcement points.
- **The filter is a GET-redirect-style nav, not a form.** Makes the filter URL bookmarkable + shareable, but a future "and filter by category" or "and filter by location" would need a real form. v1's filter set is two flat dimensions (`show=active|archived` + `requires_checkout=yes`); when there are 4+ filters, switch to a form with a Reset button. Same posture as the dashboard's two filter forms.

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — R1:**

- **Overdue checkouts is a placeholder showing 0.** C-series isn't built yet, so the widget can't surface a real number. Pinning the test-id `dashboard-overdue-checkouts` now means C-series doesn't have to re-template; the trade-off is that the dashboard reads as "complete" but one widget is informational only. Documented in self-critique. DoD #7 ticking is gated on this being real.
- **Total inventory value uses `SUM(qty_remaining * unit_cost)` directly** rather than calling the existing `open_value(db, item)` engine helper. The engine helper is per-item — looping through every active item to call it would be O(N) round-trips. The dashboard query is one round-trip; the arithmetic is identical. Trade-off: the same formula now lives in two places (here + in the engine). Acceptable; if the formula ever needs to change, both will be updated. Same pragmatic posture as `_is_leaf` duplicated between `items.py` and `field_defs.py`.
- **COGS subquery uses `IN (SELECT DISTINCT movement_id FROM cost_layer_consumptions)`** which on Postgres is fine but on SQLite walks the consumption table. For tens of thousands of movements this is still sub-millisecond on SQLite. If it ever becomes a hot path, a denormalised "is_consuming" boolean on `stock_movements` (set by the engine on consume) would close the gap — out of scope for v1.
- **Date range is end-inclusive, start-inclusive.** The route resolves `[start 00:00 UTC, end+1 00:00 UTC)` so the user's "from 2026-05-01 to 2026-05-07" picks up movements right through 2026-05-07 23:59:59 UTC. Documented inline in `_cogs`. The form input is `<input type="date">` so the user can't submit a time-of-day; making the range inclusive matches the intuitive read.
- **Top-days clamping is silent (no flash)** — a stale `?top_days=99999` link lands on the default-30-day view rather than a 400. Same posture as M6's pagination clamping. The trade-off is the user might not notice they got a different window than they asked for. The form input pre-fills with the *coerced* value, so the user sees the actual window. Acceptable.
- **No `?top_limit=` param.** The top-consumed table is hard-LIMIT 10. A power user might want top-25; we don't expose the knob. Premature; if real users ask for it, add it as a 5-line follow-up.
- **No item / supplier / category filtering on top consumed or COGS.** A workshop manager might want "COGS for raw materials only" or "top-consumed in this taxonomy node". Out of scope for R1; that's R2-R3 territory. The current widget is the one MISSION §3 enumerates — broad strokes, not slice-and-dice.
- **The forms submit GET requests with both params encoded.** Each form carries the *other* param as a hidden input so submitting one preserves the other. Trade-off: the user can't reset by leaving the field blank (the hidden input ships the previous value). To reset, they navigate to `/admin/dashboard` directly. Acceptable for v1; a "Reset" button would be a nice polish.
- **Decimal coercion uses `Decimal(str(total))` for the all-zero-rows path.** SQLite returns the integer literal `0` for `coalesce(sum(...), 0)` when no rows match. `Decimal(0)` works but the type signature says it accepts `Decimal | float | str | tuple[int, Sequence[int], int]`. The `str()` round-trip is defensive and produces an exact decimal string (`"0"`). On Postgres the column-typed sum yields a Decimal directly and we return early. Acceptable.
- **No CSV export.** R5 is the export slice. The user reading the dashboard today can't download numbers; they have to copy from the page. Out of scope for R1.
- **`_parse_cogs_date` is a duplicate of `app/purchase_orders.py::_parse_optional_date`** (same shape, different field-name parameter). Two callers, six lines each — extraction would save ~6 lines but introduce a `_validators.py` module that's used by exactly two callers. Same posture as `_parse_non_negative_decimal_required` duplicated between `purchase_orders.py` and `movements.py`. Flagged for extraction once a third caller arrives.
- **Five queries on every GET, no caching.** The route runs five aggregations on every request. At v1 scale (tens of POs, hundreds of items, thousands of movements) this is sub-100ms. If it ever shows up in monitoring as a hot path, the right fix is in-memory caching with a short TTL or a denormalised "dashboard summary" row — out of scope for v1 (MISSION §5 is intentionally cache-less).
- **No widget for "stock take variance trend" or other R-series widgets.** R4 (variance trend) and R5 (CSV export) are queued for follow-up slices. R1 covers the four DoD #7 figures; R2-R5 add the deeper reports.
- **Workshop hitting `/admin/dashboard` directly gets a 403 page.** That's correct (server-side enforcement), but the friendlier UX would be to redirect them to `/` with a flash. Conservative: 403 is the standard posture across this codebase (suppliers / locations / taxonomy etc. all 403 Workshop). Same posture as PO routes. Pinned by `test_workshop_get_is_403`.

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — PO5:**

- **Cost is required when received > 0 but blank-received with cost typed is silently dropped.** A user could fill the cost field for a line they then leave at received=0, expecting the cost to be remembered when they come back to receive it. Today the cost is not persisted to the line on a no-op submit (only the actual receive path writes anything). The form's pre-fill from `expected_unit_cost` makes this less of a problem (the operator's typed value gets overwritten by the next form render). Acceptable for v1; flagged as a polish if real users complain about losing typed values across draft submissions.
- **No correction path for a wrong-cost receipt.** Once a cost layer is written via PO5, the engine treats it as immutable (M1 contract). If the operator typed `2.00` instead of `2.50`, today's only path is a manual stock-out (consume FIFO from that layer) + manual stock-in (record at 2.50) — which leaves a trail in the audit log but adds two movements. A "correct this receipt" route would let the operator amend the layer in place, but the immutability contract means we'd really have to consume + re-receive anyway. Documented; v1 expectation is that the operator types carefully and uses M4 adjustments for corrections.
- **Receive form shows outstanding for every line, but doesn't enforce "all-or-nothing".** A multi-line PO can be partially received line-by-line over many transactions. That's by design (the supplier might send line A on Monday and line B on Friday) but it means the audit log can have many `purchase_order.received` rows for one PO. Acceptable for v1; the line-level state on the PO row plus the cumulative status is the canonical summary, the audit log is the breakdown. Flagged for R-series reporting: a PO history report should aggregate `purchase_order.received` rows per PO.
- **Over-receipt is a hard reject, not an "edit qty_ordered first" prompt.** The route 400s with "cannot receive more than ordered (ordered N, received M, requested K)" — the operator has to navigate to the edit form (which is gated on draft status) to bump qty_ordered, but a sent PO can't be edited. So in v1, "I received 110 of an order for 100" goes through manual stock-in (M2) for the +10. Documented in self-critique. A future path could allow PO line edits in the sent / partially_received states for "qty_ordered up only" — would need a new audit shape and a route surface — out of scope for v1.
- **`stock_movements.po_id` migration uses `batch_alter_table` even on Postgres.** Alembic's `batch_alter_table` is a no-op on backends that natively support `ALTER TABLE … ADD CONSTRAINT` (it falls through to a regular `op.create_foreign_key` on Postgres). Verified by reading Alembic docs; SQLite compat is the driver, Postgres parity is preserved. The migration runs on both backends without backend-specific branching.
- **`actual_unit_cost` audit value is the user-typed string** (`"2.50"`) not the column-quantised string (`"2.5000"`). Inconsistent with prior PO/cost audit shapes which carry the column-quantised representation. Pragmatic: the operator's *intent* is what should land in the audit log for a future "what did the operator type" view, and the column-quantised value is reachable via `cost_layer.unit_cost` joined back through `movement_id`. Documented; if a future R-series report wants a uniform shape, the audit reader can re-quantise on read.
- **Per-line dynamic form keys are read via `await request.form()`** — same pattern as PO2b's edit + items.py's create / update. The receive route is `async def`. Lines aren't known at function-signature time. Acceptable; documented in route docstring.
- **No optimistic-concurrency / ETag check.** Two operators receiving against the same PO simultaneously could both read `qty_received=5`, both submit `received=5`, and both validate against `5+5 <= 10`. The DB doesn't prevent this. The audit log records both transactions. Acceptable for v1 (one warehouse worker per PO is the real-world scale); flagged for future if user feedback says it's a problem. The fix shape (an `If-Match: <po.updated_at>` header) is the same as PO2b's flagged race.
- **No "preview / dry run" mode.** A receive form submission either commits or rejects. A future feature could show "this would create N movements + flip the status to X" before the user clicks final-submit — mostly useful for big multi-line POs where the operator wants to double-check before committing. Out of scope for v1; the bare 400 on validation failure is the v1 confirmation surface.
- **No JS confirm before "Record receipt"**. A misclick commits the transaction. Could add an HTMX confirm or a JS `confirm()` step. Conservative: no confirm in v1; the audit log preserves the action and a follow-up M4 adjustment can correct an over-typed receipt qty (within the same PO's available outstanding). Same posture as PO2b's cancel button.
- **The receive-link block is a paragraph link, not a primary CTA button.** Compared to PO2b's "Save changes" submit and PO4's "Send to supplier" submit, the receive link reads as a navigation hint. The form lives behind the link (one extra click). Could promote the link to a button-shaped CTA, or inline the receive form directly on the detail page (which would require splitting the bimodal template into a third branch). Acceptable for v1; the multi-step flow (detail → receive form → submit → back to detail) is the standard form pattern in this codebase.
- **No e2e walk for the partial-receive case.** The single e2e walk only exercises the full-receive path (qty=120 of qty_ordered=120). The integration suite covers the partial-receive path exhaustively (`TestPOReceiveHappyPathPartial` 3 tests). A second e2e walk for partial would be redundant given the integration coverage. Documented; queued for a polish slice if real-user feedback says the partial-receive path needs walk-level coverage.
- **`_parse_non_negative_decimal_required` is a duplicate of `app/movements.py::_parse_non_negative_decimal`.** Lives in `purchase_orders.py` because the import direction (purchase_orders → movements) doesn't exist today and the helper is six lines of code. Acceptable duplication; if a third caller appears, extract to a `_validators.py` module. Same pattern as `_is_leaf` duplicated between `items.py` and `field_defs.py`.

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — PO4:**

- **Delivery is synchronous on the request thread.** A real SMTP
  conversation can take 200ms-2s. For tens of POs in v1 this is fine
  (operators send POs one at a time after reviewing each); a future
  scheduler-driven "resend stuck POs" job would block one request per
  delivery attempt. APScheduler is already in scope per MISSION §5; queueing
  the deliveries on an in-process thread pool would isolate the latency
  but adds a new failure mode (delivery-after-commit means the audit row
  could outlive a delivery failure). Acceptable for v1; flagged as a perf
  follow-up if it ever bites.
- **`SmtpEmailBackend` is untested.** The integration suite exercises only
  `ConsoleEmailBackend`. SMTP is a thin wrapper over `smtplib.SMTP` +
  `email.message.EmailMessage` — both stdlib, both well-trodden — so the
  failure mode is "I forgot to call `starttls`" or "I forgot to login",
  which a real-SMTP integration test would catch. The pragmatic path is to
  defer that test to deployment (a manual once-off sanity check against
  Mailpit / Mailtrap during the prod-deploy slice). Documented as a
  deployment-time TODO; queued for a P-series slice.
- **Delivery happens before the DB flip.** If `SmtpEmailBackend.send`
  raises, no status change and no audit row is written — tested via the
  validation-error path's outbox + audit assertions, but the SMTP-raise
  case isn't directly covered (would require a backend that raises). A
  future test could substitute a `RaisingEmailBackend` via a
  `monkeypatch`. Defer for v1 — the contract is the same as M3's
  insufficient-stock atomic-on-raise pattern, which is exhaustively
  tested at the engine level.
- **Audit shape's `to_email` could rot.** If the supplier's email
  changes after the PO was sent, the audit row still carries the old
  address. That's the *correct* behaviour for an audit log (it records
  what was true at the time of sending). The supplier table joins back
  via `supplier_id` for "what's the current address". No change needed,
  but flagged in case future reporting wants a join-back path.
- **Subject line is hardcoded `"Purchase Order #{id} from UC"`.** Real
  procurement emails often include the supplier's PO number conventions
  ("PO-2026-001"), the requester's name, etc. Out of scope for v1;
  belongs to the future "supplier address / template" polish slice.
- **Body HTML is built by string concatenation** rather than via a
  Jinja template. The body is short (4-5 paragraphs) and the call site
  is one route. Templating the body would add a new template file +
  context dict for ~6 lines of HTML — net negative. If the email
  surface grows (PO5 receipt notification, R-series report emails),
  flip it to a Jinja template at that point. Acceptable.
- **No "blind copy" of UC's own staff on outgoing emails.** Some shops
  cc `purchasing@uc.test` on every PO so there's an internal record.
  Out of scope for v1 (the audit log + the saved PO are the internal
  record); flagged as a future setting (`SMTP_BCC_INTERNAL`).
- **`pyproject.toml` doesn't list `smtplib` / `email` because they're
  stdlib.** No new external dependency was needed; reportlab is the only
  PDF dep. The `premailer` dep listed in `pyproject.toml` is unused so
  far — flagged for a future cleanup if it stays unused after PO5.
- **The `_reset_email_outbox` autouse fixture lives in
  `test_purchase_orders_routes.py` only.** When other modules start
  using the email backend (e.g. R-series report emails), the fixture
  should move into `tests/conftest.py` so every test gets a clean
  outbox. Premature today — only one caller — but flagged.
- **Send route does not validate `app_settings.smtp_from`.** When the
  backend is `console`, sender is metadata only. When the backend is
  `smtp`, an empty `smtp_from` would result in a malformed
  `From:` header and probably a delivery rejection. Settings already
  defaults `smtp_from = "inventory@example.com"`. Flagged but
  acceptable; the failure mode is "delivery rejected at send-time"
  which is loud, not silent.
- **Re-downloading the PDF after sending is allowed (PO3's status
  guard accepts every non-cancelled status).** A future "freeze the
  PDF at send-time" feature would store the PDF bytes on the PO row
  (or a sibling table) so the supplier and UC can always agree on
  exactly what was sent. Out of scope for v1; the regenerated PDF is
  deterministic enough (same PO row → same bytes) that drift is
  unlikely.
- **`_require_draft`'s message ("PO is {status}; only drafts can be
  edited") is reused for the send route.** "Edited" is technically
  incorrect for a status-change verb, but the user-visible difference
  (a sent PO is rejected with the same wording) is small. Could split
  into a `_require_draft_for_action(action_name)` helper that
  parameterises the verb. Three lines saved across two routes today;
  not worth the abstraction yet.

---



**Self-critique notes (rolling) — PO3:**

- **Reportlab not WeasyPrint, despite the previous next-slice plan leaning
  WeasyPrint.** WeasyPrint can't import on this env (missing native libs).
  MISSION §5 lists both options ("WeasyPrint or reportlab. Pick one and
  stick with it") — switching from one to the other is *within* §5 not
  outside it. Removed `weasyprint` from `pyproject.toml` so the choice is
  unambiguous. Tradeoff: PDF layout is hand-built (no HTML template),
  duplicates some structure from `purchase_order_detail.html`. Acceptable
  for a printed-form audience. If a future polish pass wants HTML→PDF
  fidelity (letterhead, complex layouts), revisit by installing WeasyPrint's
  native deps + flipping the implementation. Documented in
  `app/pdf.py`'s module docstring.
- **Stream compression disabled for byte-searchable tests.** The renderer
  calls `canvas.setPageCompression(0)`. This makes the PDF ~3× larger
  (uncompressed) but POs are tiny single-page documents in v1, so the
  practical size is still under 10 KB. The test suite searches the byte
  stream directly (e.g. `b"PDF-CONTENT-1" in resp.content`) instead of
  pulling in `pypdf` or `pdfminer.six`. If we ever re-enable compression,
  tests will need a proper extractor — flagged in the module docstring.
  This is the kind of "tests pin the implementation" wart MISSION §8 warns
  against, but the alternative (an extra dependency for byte-extraction)
  has worse lifetime cost.
- **Layout is single-page only.** A PO with > ~30 lines will have line
  cells overflow off the bottom. Reportlab's `Canvas` doesn't auto-paginate
  — you have to drive `showPage()` yourself when y drops below a margin.
  Out of scope for PO3 (the operator's first PO will have ~5 lines from
  PO1's RD-LOW seed). Self-critique flag for a follow-up.
- **No supplier address block / UC letterhead.** The MISSION mentions
  "Send PO via email (PDF attachment) to supplier" but doesn't enumerate
  what info the PDF must carry. Today's `Supplier` columns are name +
  email + phone + notes — no address. A real supplier-printable PDF needs
  an address, a delivery address, and UC's letterhead. Addressed in PO4's
  email design (the email body can carry the to-address) and / or as a
  follow-up `Supplier.address` slice. Out of scope here.
- **Em-dash encoding in tests is brittle.** `TestPOPdfContent::
  test_unpriced_line_shows_em_dash_for_total` asserts the literal byte
  sequence `b"Total: \\227"` — that's the PDF stream's octal escape for
  WinAnsi byte 0x97 (em-dash). If reportlab ever switches default font /
  encoding, the test breaks loudly. Acceptable: the test pins the *current*
  encoding which is what we want for now; flipping fonts is a deliberate
  decision that should require a test update.
- **`Total: 30.00000000` (8-decimal grand total)** is mathematically right
  but visually noisy. `Decimal("12.0000") * Decimal("2.5000")` = scale 8.
  A `quantize(Decimal("0.01"))` on the grand total would give `30.00`, which
  is what a supplier wants to read. Out of scope for PO3 (the test pins
  the current shape; cleanup is a 3-line follow-up). Self-critique flag.
- **`target="_blank"` opens a tab; the e2e test fetches via `request.get`
  rather than asserting the new tab loads.** Chromium's built-in PDF viewer
  doesn't fire the same `domcontentloaded` event a normal HTML page does,
  so `context.expect_page()` + `wait_for_load_state()` is flaky. Using
  `mgr_page.request.get(href)` is more deterministic and rides the same
  session cookie. The tradeoff is we don't actually exercise the click;
  the link's presence + the `request.get` of the same URL is verified, but
  the *binding* between the click and the request is not. A future polish
  pass could use Playwright's download API or a `domcontentloaded`-with-
  timeout fallback. Acceptable today.
- **No "Open in new tab" hint to the user.** The link's `target="_blank"`
  is a behaviour, not a label. Some browsers show an icon, but there's no
  text affordance. Out of scope for PO3; queued for a P2 accessibility pass.
- **PDF is generated synchronously on the request thread.** For tens of
  lines this is well under a second, but a pathological 500-line PO could
  block the event loop briefly. APScheduler / a background-render queue is
  out of scope for v1 (MISSION §5 explicitly says no Celery / Redis); a
  future fix would be to render on a thread pool via `run_in_executor` —
  noted as a perf follow-up if real POs ever get that big.
- **The route's `created_at` rendering uses `created_at.date().isoformat()`**
  rather than the full timestamp. POs are typically dated by day (the day
  they were created), not by minute. The on-screen detail page shows the
  full ISO timestamp; the PDF shows only the date. Slight inconsistency
  but the right user-facing posture for each surface. Documented inline.
- **No PDF link for cancelled POs.** Both the route (400) and the template
  (link hidden) agree — cancelled POs have nothing to send. Defensive: if
  a stale tab POSTs cancel and then GETs `/pdf` directly, the route still
  rejects. Pinned by `test_cancelled_po_is_400`.
- **`render_po_pdf` is pure (no DB / Request / HTTPException) but takes
  view dicts, not the SQLAlchemy models.** Means the route does the
  load-and-shape, then the helper does the render — clean separation, but
  there's no type guarantee on the dict shape. A `TypedDict` could pin it.
  Acceptable for a single caller; if PO4 reuses the helper, that's the
  time to add the TypedDicts.

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — PO2b:**

- **No optimistic-concurrency / ETag / version check.** Two managers editing the same draft simultaneously race, last-writer wins. Acceptable for v1 (drafts are typically a one-person operation; the audit log preserves both edits if they happen). A `If-Match` header against `po.updated_at` would close the race but adds a new failure mode. Defer until user feedback says it's a real problem.
- **`update_purchase_order` is `async def`; the others in this module are sync.** Inconsistent. Justified by `await request.form()` for the per-line dynamic keys (line ids aren't known at function-signature time) — same precedent as `app/items.py`'s `create_item` / `update_item`. Could refactor by walking the existing helpers, but the inconsistency is local and well-documented in the route docstring.
- **Cancel uses a separate POST route + form.** Could be consolidated as a hidden field on the edit form (`<button name="action" value="cancel">`). Two routes is more explicit and matches the existing audit-action split (`updated` vs `cancelled` are two distinct events). The two-form pattern is also more accessible — one big submit + one explicit destructive button.
- **`po-line-qty-received` cell renders `0.0000` on every line until PO5.** Carried forward from PO2's self-critique. Now visible on both the read-only and the edit-mode renders. The qty_received column is *not* editable (it's set by PO5 receipts), correctly — so the read-only cell on the edit form is a small inconsistency. Acceptable.
- **No "uncancel" route.** Once cancelled, a draft is permanently in that state — operator must create a new draft. MISSION §3 doesn't require unbreaking; the audit log preserves the state machine. Fine.
- **Missing-line-key triggers 400.** A user with a stale tab (line was deleted by another manager, or the line set was modified) would see a bare 400. Edge case; the dashboard / supplier group is the source of line sets, so a stale tab is rare. Could fall back to silent-skip-the-line, but error-loud is safer. Pinned by `test_missing_line_qty_field_is_400`.
- **The audit `lines` shape uses parallel `before` / `after` lists**, not a single combined "delta" list. Picked for consistency with the rest of the audit log (everything else uses parallel before/after dicts). Could reshape to `{lines: [{line_id, qty_ordered: {before, after}}]}` for compactness, but parallel-lists matches the rest. Pro/con tradeoff.
- **No-op submit flashes "no changes".** Could be silent. Explicit feedback is clearer (the user knows the form did submit) and pinned by `test_no_op_submit_writes_no_audit`. Self-critique flag — "saved" vs "no changes" copy is informal, may want a polish pass when R-series lands.
- **Status-guard error message is bare-400-page** ("PO is sent; only drafts can be edited"). Same posture as every other validation 400 outside M3 / M4's data-dependent stock-shortage carve-out. The status check is non-data-dependent — typing the form again won't help; the only fix is to navigate. Bare 400 is the right posture.
- **`expected_date` is rendered with `<input type="date">`** — relies on browser support for the picker. Falls back to text input on older browsers. The `_parse_optional_date` validation accepts strict ISO format, which the picker emits. Acceptable.
- **The cancel button has no "are you sure?" confirmation.** A misclick destroys the draft (well, marks it cancelled — drafts can't be uncancelled). Could add a JS `confirm()` or an HTMX swap with a confirmation step. Conservative: no confirmation in v1; the audit log preserves the action and the operator can re-draft. Self-critique flag for a polish pass.
- **PO list page doesn't show a `cancelled` filter shortcut.** The user can pick `cancelled` from the filter dropdown. Not a regression — same as before PO2b.
- **Existing PO2 tests `test_lines_render_in_sku_order_with_correct_cells` and `test_null_expected_cost_shows_empty_marker` were flipped from `POStatus.DRAFT` to `POStatus.SENT`.** Necessary because the read-only test-ids those tests assert (`po-line-qty-ordered`, `po-line-cost-empty`) now only appear on non-draft renders. PO2b's `TestPODetailRenderDelta` covers the draft branch separately. The flip is documented inline so a future reader understands why those tests use a non-draft status.

---

**Self-critique notes (rolling) — PO2:**

- **Editing per-line `qty_ordered` / `expected_unit_cost` is deferred to PO2b.** MISSION §3 says "Expected unit cost on a PO line is editable by the user creating the PO" — PO2 stores the column but doesn't yet expose an edit surface. The PO is created with auto-defaults from PO1's data and read back on the detail page. PO2b will add the `POST /admin/purchase-orders/{po_id}` route + edit form on the same detail page. The split keeps PO2's audit shape simple (`purchase_order.created` only); PO2b adds `purchase_order.updated` with the sparse-line-diff problem worked through. Without PO2b, MISSION §3's editability requirement isn't satisfied — DoD #6 cannot tick yet.
- **No "cancel draft PO" route.** A draft PO created in error has no UI to undo. The status enum carries `cancelled` for forward compatibility, but no route writes it. Acceptable for one iteration (the operator can ignore the draft until PO2b's edit form or a future cancel route lands), but the "wrong supplier clicked twice" scenario leaves orphan drafts. Queued for PO2b alongside the edit form (a "Cancel this draft" button would be a 3-line follow-up).
- **Stale-POST race condition is not de-duplicated.** Two managers clicking Draft PO for the same supplier within seconds creates two draft POs covering the same items. Acceptable in v1 (each draft is independent and editable; the audit log preserves who drafted which); flagged for future. A "no draft for this supplier currently exists" guard would close the race but adds a new failure mode (the user sees 400 and can't draft until the existing one is sent / cancelled). Defer until user feedback says it's a real problem.
- **`qty_received` cell renders `0.0000` on every line until PO5.** The detail view shows the column unconditionally. Visually noisy in PO2 (every line has the same value), but the column is part of MISSION §6's data model and PO5 needs the cell to be in the same place. Better to render it now than re-template in PO5.
- **`po-list-empty` shows the same copy for an unfiltered empty list and a filtered-but-no-matches list.** Filtering by `?status_filter=sent` on a system with only drafts shows "No purchase orders yet." which technically isn't true. The secondary signal is the filter dropdown still showing "sent". Minor UX nit; queued for a small copy tweak ("No purchase orders matching this filter") without re-templating.
- **`expected_unit_cost` defaults to the most recent layer regardless of `qty_remaining`.** A fully-consumed layer is still the most recent unit-cost signal — the lookup doesn't filter by `qty_remaining > 0`. By design: a layer with `qty_remaining=0` is still the truth about *what we last paid*; the operator can edit if the market has moved. Pinned by `test_newest_layer_picked_when_multiple` (oldest 2.00 + newest 3.00 → 3.00 wins) but no test specifically covers "fully drained newest layer still wins" — the `_seed_layer` helper creates fresh layers on every seed, so the path is implicitly exercised but not explicitly named. Flagged for an explicit test in PO2b's batch.
- **`_count_lines` runs once per PO row in the list view.** `O(N)` queries on the list page. Acceptable for tens of POs in v1 (the loop's expected scale per MISSION §4 "list views with 5,000 items must paginate" — the *items* list, not POs; PO counts will be much smaller). For thousands of POs the right fix is a single `func.count` grouped query or a denormalised `line_count` column. Defer until perf shows up as a problem.
- **The CASCADE delete on `purchase_order_lines.po_id` is ahead of any UI**. PO2 has no hard-delete path; the cascade is a forward-looking parity for a future "destroy a never-sent draft" UX. Could have used RESTRICT here for parity with the rest of the app — chose CASCADE because the natural mental model is "lines are owned by their PO; destroying the PO destroys the lines". Audit log preservation isn't affected — the audit row is independent of the PO. If the team disagrees this can flip in a follow-up migration without data loss.
- **`status` column has both Python-side default and `server_default='draft'`.** SQLAlchemy needs both for a NOT NULL string column to satisfy "the row writes if the model didn't set it" + "the SQL default writes if a hand-crafted INSERT didn't set it". Belt-and-braces; matches `current_qty` / `reorder_threshold` / `reorder_qty` on Items.
- **Audit `lines` is a list-of-dicts, not a sparse-diff dict.** That's the natural shape for a creation event (no "before"). PO2b's `purchase_order.updated` will need a different shape — sparse line-level diff (`{"lines": [{"line_id": N, "before": {...}, "after": {...}}, ...]}` or similar). Don't pre-design PO2b's shape; just flagged that the two events will have different `lines` representations, which is fine because they're keyed by `action`.
- **No supplier filter on the PO list view.** Status is filterable; supplier is not. A workshop with 50 suppliers and a long PO list will scroll. Adding a supplier dropdown filter is the obvious next step but it's also a reporting concern that R-series can take cleanly.
- **`/admin/purchase-orders/{po_id}` doesn't carry an "Edit" link**. PO2b will add it, gated on `status == draft`. PO2's detail page links to "Back to all POs" + "Reorder dashboard" only — both reads. Workshop is excluded from the route entirely (MISSION §3 "cannot manage POs"); PO2 doesn't expose the link, so there's nothing to gate.

---

## Next slice

**C4 — Manager "currently out / overdue" view.** The last gate before DoD #4 ticks. Adds a single read-only route — likely `GET /admin/checkouts` for **Manager + Office** (Workshop hidden — the workshop user already sees per-item status blocks; cross-item "who has what" is an oversight tool) — that lists every open `Checkout` row joined to its item + actor + (optional) item_unit, ordered with overdue first then by `checked_out_at` desc. Two filter tabs: `?show=open` (default — `returned_at IS NULL`) and `?show=overdue` (open AND `expected_return < now()`). Per-row: item name + sku, unit serial (or "—" for qty-tracked), holder email, checked-out-at, expected-return (or "—"), days-overdue badge when applicable. New `nav-checkouts` link in `base.html` (Manager / Office / Admin; Workshop hidden). The dashboard's `dashboard-overdue-checkouts` widget (placeholder=0 since R1) gets wired up to the same query, so DoD #7 also moves a step closer. Probable size: 1 iteration; new route + new template + small dashboard wiring; e2e walk creates an overdue checkout (backdated `checked_out_at`/`expected_return`) and asserts the row appears in both the dashboard widget and the new view.

Alternates: **R5** (CSV export on every list view — DoD #7 polish); **PDF polish** (quantise the grand total to scale 2 + multipage support); **`Supplier.address` column** for PO PDFs; **per-unit transfer for I3 unique-tracked items**; **SC1** (scan-mode page — opens DoD #3 toward unticking).

---

## Backlog (rough order of attack)

These are sliced small. Each should be one to three iterations of work. Reorder as needed; the only hard rule is that earlier slices should unblock later ones.

### Foundations
- **F1** Project skeleton and verification harness *(see Next slice)*
- **F2** Google SSO login + pending-state user model + role enum
- **F3** Audit log infrastructure (append-only, hooks for state changes)
- **F4** Base layout, navigation, role-aware menu, HTMX wired in

### Settings (Manager-owned)
- **S1** Suppliers CRUD
- **S2** Locations CRUD
- **S3** Taxonomy: top-level categories CRUD
- **S4** Taxonomy: sub-categories under a category
- **S5** Taxonomy: custom field defs per leaf node (text, number, decimal, date, boolean, select, multiselect)
- **S6** Field schema versioning behaviour (existing items keep values; new edits enforce current schema; deletes hide-not-purge)

### Items
- **I1** Item core fields + create/edit/archive against a chosen leaf node
- **I2** Item custom fields rendered + validated from the leaf node's schema
- **I3** Unique-tracked items: `item_units` table, per-unit serial labels
- **I4** QR code generation + printable label view

### Stock movements & cost
