- **M1** `cost_layers` + `cost_layer_consumptions` tables and the FIFO consumption engine (pure logic, well-tested before any UI)
- **M2** Manual stock-in form (qty + unit cost → creates layer + "in" movement)
- **M3** Manual stock-out form (qty → consumes layers FIFO → records consumptions + "out" movement)
- **M4** Adjustment movements (positive creates layer, negative consumes FIFO; reason required)
- **M5** Transfer between locations (no cost change)
- **M6** Item detail page: current qty, open layers, full movement history

### Scanning
- **SC1** Scan-mode page (USB scanner: focused input, action picker, qty entry)
- **SC2** Camera-based scanning on phone/tablet (use a maintained JS QR lib via CDN)
- **SC3** Bulk scan mode for stock takes

### Check-out / check-in
- **C1** Per-item `requires_checkout` flag
- **C2** Check-out flow (assign to user, expected return)
- **C3** Check-in flow + condition note
- **C4** Manager view: currently-out + overdue list

### Stock takes
- **ST1** Stock take scheduling and scope (by node, by location, custom set)
- **ST2** Stock take session UI (start, count, see variance, commit adjustments)
- **ST3** Variance reports + linkage from adjustment movements back to the stock take

### Reorder & POs
- **PO1** Reorder dashboard (items below threshold, grouped by supplier)
- **PO2** Draft PO from low-stock selection (lines with expected unit cost editable)
- **PO3** PO PDF generation
- **PO4** Email PO to supplier (SMTP, console backend in dev)
- **PO5** Receive against PO (full / partial), enter actual unit cost per line, create cost layers and "in" movements

### Reporting
- **R1** Dashboard: total inventory value (from open layers), low-stock count, overdue checkouts
- **R2** Top consumed items over a window
- **R3** Cost-of-goods-consumed for a date range
- **R4** Stock-take variance trend
- **R5** CSV export on every list view

### Polish & deploy
- **P1** Mobile responsiveness pass (workshop tablets, 10" target)
- **P2** Accessibility pass (keyboard nav, contrast, focus states)
- **P3** Postgres parity: run full test suite against Postgres in CI
- **P4** Deployment config (Fly.io or Render) + production env handling
- **P5** README finalisation: setup, deploy, configure SSO, common workflows

---

## Definition of Done tracker

From MISSION.md §7. Tick only when verified by tests AND a manual sanity-check.

- [ ] 1. New user signs in with Google → pending → Admin assigns role → access works.
- [x] 2. Manager defines taxonomy + custom fields. Admin creates items in those nodes (qty + unique). Required fields enforced. Archive/unarchive works. *(Ticked iteration 16 / I3a. Backed by S3 + S4 + S5 + I1a/b + I2 + I3 + I3a. Integration: 100+ tests across `test_items_routes.py` + `test_item_units_routes.py` + `test_field_defs_routes.py` covering Admin and Manager paths, every required-field 400, archive/unarchive idempotency, custom-field type matrix. E2E: two walks in `test_items_e2e.py` — Manager walks taxonomy + field defs + qty-tracked + flip-to-unique + multi-unit cycle; Admin walks category + qty-tracked + flip-to-unique + unit cycle.)*
- [ ] 3. Workshop user scans QR (USB on desktop AND camera on mobile), records in/out/adjust in two interactions. Stock-ins record unit cost.
- [ ] 4. Workshop user checks out / in tools and moulds. Manager sees who has what + overdue.
- [ ] 5. Office user runs a stock take end-to-end. Variances hit audit. Positive adj. requires cost; negative consumes FIFO.
- [x] 6. Reorder dashboard → draft PO → edit expected costs → send PDF email → mark received with actual costs → cost layers created, valuation updates. *(Ticked iteration 29 / PO5. Backed by PO1 (reorder dashboard) + PO2 (draft create) + PO2b (edit + cancel) + PO3 (PDF) + PO4 (email send) + PO5 (receive with FIFO cost layers). - [ ] 7. Dashboard shows value (FIFO), low stock, overdue, top consumed, COGS over date range.
- [ ] 8. Every state change in audit log with actor + timestamp. Audit log not editable.

| 30 | R1 — Reporting dashboard with FIFO valuation, low-stock count, top consumed, COGS (DoD #7) | `666e7c1` | First link in DoD #7's chain. New module `app/dashboard.py` with one route `GET /admin/dashboard` for **Manager + Office** (Admin via the bypass; Workshop + pending 403 — MISSION §3 "Workshop... cannot see aggregated cost data or reports"). Read-only — no mutations, no audit, no movement type, no new tables. **Aggregations** (each is a single round-trip): total inventory value = `SUM(qty_remaining * unit_cost)` across active items' open `cost_layers` rows (joined to `items` filtered `archived_at IS NULL`); low-stock count = `COUNT(items)` where `archived_at IS NULL AND current_qty <= reorder_threshold`; open POs count = `COUNT(purchase_orders)` where `status IN (draft, sent, partially_received)`; overdue checkouts = hardcoded 0 with `<small>` "checkouts not yet implemented" note (C-series will replace it; pinning the test-id `dashboard-overdue-checkouts` now means C-series doesn't have to re-template); top consumed = `SUM(qty)` over `stock_movements WHERE type=OUT AND created_at >= now() - top_days` grouped by `item_id`, joined to `items`, ordered desc, LIMIT 10 (window via `?top_days=N` defaulting 30; clamped `[1, 365]`; non-int / out-of-range silently coerce to default — same posture as M6 pagination); COGS = `SUM(total_cost)` over `stock_movements` where `id IN (SELECT DISTINCT movement_id FROM cost_layer_consumptions) AND created_at BETWEEN cogs_start AND cogs_end+1d` (consumption-row subquery covers OUT + negative-adjustment ADJUSTMENT — both go through `consume_fifo`; adjustment-increase has no consumption row so it's correctly excluded; IN has total_cost set but no consumption row; TRANSFER has neither). The COGS date range is end-inclusive (resolves to `[start 00:00 UTC, end+1 00:00 UTC)`). Default range: last 30 days. Bad-format ISO date 400. **Helpers**: `_coerce_top_days(raw)` (silent coerce on bad / out-of-range), `_parse_cogs_date(raw, *, field_name)` (400 on bad format; blank → None), `_resolve_cogs_range(start, end)` (defaults end=today, start=end-30d). Five aggregation helpers (`_total_inventory_value`, `_low_stock_count`, `_open_pos_count`, `_top_consumed`, `_cogs`) are pure DB reads — no side effects, no Request, no HTTPException. **Decimal coercion**: `func.coalesce(func.sum(...), 0)` returns Decimal under SQLAlchemy's `Numeric(14,4)` round-trip but mypy types `scalar_one()` as Any; defensively branch `if isinstance(total, Decimal): return total else Decimal(str(total))`. The `Decimal(str(...))` lands when SQLite reports SUM as int (all-zero-rows case). Both paths produce a deterministic Decimal output with no precision loss. **Templates / test-ids**: new `dashboard.html` with at-a-glance card row (`dashboard-heading`, `dashboard-total-value`, `dashboard-low-stock-count`, `dashboard-open-pos-count`, `dashboard-overdue-checkouts`); top-consumed table (`dashboard-top-consumed-table` + per-row `dashboard-top-consumed-row` with `data-item-id` + cells `dashboard-top-consumed-sku` / `dashboard-top-consumed-name` / `dashboard-top-consumed-qty` / `dashboard-top-consumed-detail-link`; empty state `dashboard-top-consumed-empty`); two filter forms (`dashboard-top-days-form` + `dashboard-top-days-input` + `dashboard-top-days-submit`; `dashboard-cogs-form` + `dashboard-cogs-start-input` + `dashboard-cogs-end-input` + `dashboard-cogs-submit`); COGS card (`dashboard-cogs-amount`). Each filter form carries the *other* param as a hidden input so submitting one preserves the other's value. `base.html` gains a `nav-dashboard` link (between Home and Suppliers) visible to Admin / Manager / Office; Workshop hidden. The `aria-current` is on `path == "/admin/dashboard" or startswith("/admin/dashboard/")` (same tightening pattern as PO2's `nav-reorder` fix). **Tests** (37 new — 32 in `tests/integration/test_dashboard_routes.py` + 5 in `tests/integration/test_layout.py` + 1 e2e walk in `test_dashboard_e2e.py`): `TestDashboardRoleEnforcement` (6) — anon 401; pending 403; Workshop 403; Manager / Office / Admin 200; `TestDashboardTotalValue` (5) — empty zero; single layer `total_value="25.0000"` (10×2.50 column-quantised); multi-item sum (10×2 + 5×3 = 35); archived item's layers excluded; fully-consumed layer contributes 0 (0 + 5×3 = 15); `TestDashboardLowStockCount` (3) — zero state; positive count (2 below + 1 above-threshold = 2); archived items excluded; `TestDashboardOpenPOsCount` (2) — zero; counts draft + sent + partially_received but excludes received + cancelled (3 of 5 in seed); `TestDashboardTopConsumed` (7) — empty when no OUTs; orders by sum(qty) desc with sku-asc tiebreak (B=20 > C=10 > A=5); window excludes 100-day-old OUT (default 30-day); `?top_days=200` includes the 100-day-old OUT; `?top_days=foo` coerces to 30; `?top_days=99999` coerces to 30; TRANSFER not counted; `TestDashboardCOGS` (8) — zero with no movements; sums OUT total_cost (3×2 = "6.0000"); sums ADJUSTMENT decreases AND excludes ADJUSTMENT increases (only the 2-unit decrease counts: 2×2 = "4.0000"); IN movements not counted; default-window picks only recent OUT (6.0000); | 23 | M5 — Transfer between locations (no cost change) (DoD #3 partial, DoD #5 partial) | `33aa662` | Closes out the cost-engine call-site matrix: TRANSFER is the **only** `MovementType` that bypasses the engine, by design (no qty change → no cost change). New routes `GET /admin/items/{item_id}/transfer` + `POST /admin/items/{item_id}/transfer` mounted on the existing `app/movements.py` router for **Manager + Office + Workshop** (same matrix as M2 / M3 / M4 / M6). The route flips `item.location_id` from the current value to the user-picked target, records a `StockMovement(type=TRANSFER, total_cost=None)`, writes a `stock_movement.transfer` audit row, commits — never calls the cost engine, never creates a `CostLayer`, never writes a `CostLayerConsumption`, never mutates `item.current_qty`. Verified by three engine-isolation tests that seed a layer + run a transfer + assert the layer count + qty_remaining + current_qty are all unchanged. **Validation** (all 400 *before* any DB write — atomic): item exists (404), not archived (400), has a current `location_id` set (400 with "this item has no location yet — set one via the edit form before transferring"); `to_location_id` parses as int and references an *active* `Location` (archived rejects with "target location is not active"); `to_location_id` differs from current `location_id` (no-op transfers reject — would write a confusing audit row); `qty` parses as a positive Decimal (reuses `_parse_positive_decimal`). `reason` and `note` are optional, stripped, blank → None — same as M2 / M3; M4 differs because adjustments require attribution, transfers don't. **Audit shape**: `action="stock_movement.transfer"`, `entity_type="stock_movement"`, `entity_id=movement.id`, `before={"location_id": from_location_id}`, `after={"item_id", "qty", "from_location_id", "to_location_id", "reason", "note"}`. The `before` carries only the changed field on the *Item* (location_id), keeping the diff narrow and consistent with `item.updated`. The `after` carries the route inputs plus the resolved from/to ids so the row is self-contained for reporting (a future "by-location movement report" can read this row without joining back to movement + item). `from_location_id` appears in both `before` and `after` — that's deliberate, not a bug. **No `total_cost`, no `unit_cost`, no `source`, no `received_at`** — transfer rows don't carry any of those, consistent with the contract. **Form**: `qty` defaults to `current_qty` (most transfers are wholesale). For v1's single-location-per-item data model, the qty is informational on the movement row only — the location pointer flips wholesale regardless. Documented in the form's `<em>recorded for audit; transfers don't change current quantity or valuation</em>` hint. Partial-qty transfers across multiple "stock-by-location" rows is a v2 multi-location feature; out of scope for v1 per MISSION §3 "between locations (if multi-location is enabled)". **No in-form 400 carve-out** (unlike M3 / M4): every M5 validation error is a "user typed something wrong" case (parse error, out-of-options, same-as-current), not a data-dependent runtime error like M3's insufficient-stock. The bare-400 page is the right posture, matching every other validation 400 in the app outside M3 / M4's data-dependent stock-shortage carve-out. **M6 timeline integration**: TRANSFER rows render with no direction sign — `_attach_directions_and_breakdown`'s defensive `else` branch (already in place from M6) leaves `direction = ""` for movements that don't go through the engine. The `data-direction=""` attribute lets future styling distinguish them. The `total_cost` cell shows "—" via the existing `{% if m.total_cost is not none %}` template logic. **No layer-breakdown sub-row** appears for transfers (since the engine never wrote a consumption row for them). M6 needs zero template changes for M5. From/to location names are *not* surfaced on the timeline (they live in the audit row only) — flagged as a self-critique item for a future enrichment slice. **Templates**: new `stock_transfer_form.html` mirroring `stock_out_form.html`'s shape (header + form + recent-movements). Test-ids: `stock-transfer-form`, `stock-transfer-from-location` (read-only display of the current location label), `stock-transfer-to-location-input`, `stock-transfer-qty-input`, `stock-transfer-reason-input`, `stock-transfer-note-input`, `stock-transfer-submit`. `items_form.html` gains a fourth `data-testid="stock-transfer-link"` "Transfer →" link in the same `{% if not item.archived_at %}` block as in / out / adjust. `item_detail.html` likewise gets a `data-testid="stock-transfer-link"` action link in the same block. **Tests** (46 new = 46 integration + 1 e2e walk extension): role enforcement (10) — anon GET / POST 401, pending 403, every active role 200 GET / 303 POST; form rendering (10) — inputs + CSRF + current-location label + to-location options exclude the current AND archived rows + qty pre-fills with current_qty + recent-movements empty + 404 / 400 / item-without-location-400; validation matrix (13) — blank to_location 400, non-int 400, unknown 400, archived target 400, same-as-current 400, qty 4 cases, archived item POST 400, item-without-location POST 400, no-audit-on-failure, no-flip-on-failure across two paths (same-location reject + bad-target reject); happy path (5) — creates `StockMovement(type=TRANSFER)` with the right fields incl. total_cost=None, flips item.location_id, audit row with the right before/after shape, whitespace strip on reason, blank reason/note → None, flash includes "Transfer recorded" + both location names + item name; engine isolation (3) — no `CostLayer` / `CostLayerConsumption` / `current_qty` mutation; transfer link visibility (2) — visible for active item, hidden for archived; detail-page rendering (2) — TRANSFER row with `data-direction=""` + "—" total cost + no layer-breakdown follow-up; detail-link visibility (2) — visible / hidden the same way. E2E walk in-place extension: manager-setup step now creates two locations (`Movements From Bench`, `Movements To Storage`) and pins the item to the first; after the existing M6 detail-page leg (current_qty=75), workshop deep-links to `/transfer`, asserts the from-location shows "Movements From Bench", picks "Movements To Storage" by label, fills qty=75 + reason="end of shift", submits, asserts the flash + movement-row + flipped from-location label after the redirect (now showing "Movements To Storage"); re-visits detail and asserts 5 timeline rows + 2 layer-breakdown blocks (TRANSFER doesn't add one) + current_qty unchanged at 75.0000. Cleanup-step extension: manager archives both locations after the item + category. 836 unit+integration (was 790, +46). 10 e2e (unchanged file count; movements walk gained one new step). ruff + mypy clean (17 source files, unchanged — M5 extends `app/movements.py` in-place). |

| 17 | M1 — `cost_layers` + `cost_layer_consumptions` + `stock_movements` + FIFO consumption engine (DoD #5, #6 prerequisite) | `2cd2c6c` | Pure-logic slice — no routes, no UI, no e2e. New `app/cost_engine.py` exposes `record_receipt`, `consume_fifo`, `open_value`, and `InsufficientStockError`. The engine is the **single owner** of `item.current_qty`, `cost_layers.qty_remaining`, and `stock_movements.total_cost` going forward — every M2-M6 / PO5 / ST-series route must call into it rather than mutate those columns directly. New ORM models in `app/models.py`: `StockMovement` (with `MovementType` enum: in/out/adjustment/transfer), `CostLayer` (with `CostLayerSource` enum: po_receipt/manual_in/positive_adjustment), `CostLayerConsumption`. Migration `0010_create_cost_layers_and_movements.py` adds the three tables in dependency order (movements first, then layers, then consumptions — consumptions FK into both layers and movements). **Schema deviation from MISSION §6**: `stock_movements.po_id` and `stock_take_id` are plain `Integer` columns with **no FK constraint** in M1, because `purchase_orders` and `stock_takes` don't exist yet. The FK constraint is a one-line addition in PO2 / ST1's migrations. Documented on the model. **No `archived_at` on any of the three new tables**: they're append-only by mission (§3 "Cost layer history is part of the audit trail and cannot be edited. Corrections are made via new movements"). The engine *does* mutate `cost_layers.qty_remaining` on consumption — that's the one exception, called out in the model docstring (running balance vs frozen received qty). **No DB-level immutability triggers** on the new tables (the audit-log triggers stay scoped to `audit_log` only): the engine is the only writer, and the route layer (M2+) won't expose UPDATE/DELETE paths. If a future "data correction" backdoor is ever added, that's the time to add triggers. **Engine contract**: caller creates the `StockMovement` row, flushes for id, then calls into the engine. Engine takes the movement as input (rather than constructing one) so the route layer owns actor / reason / type / note / po_id wiring. Engine sets `movement.total_cost` as a side effect. Engine raises `ValueError` for input violations (qty <= 0, unit_cost < 0, unflushed movement) and `InsufficientStockError(item_id, requested, available)` for over-consume. **Atomicity** of `consume_fifo`: the available-qty pre-check happens before any mutation, so a raise leaves the DB exactly as it was — verified by `test_over_consumption_is_atomic`. **FIFO order**: `(received_at ASC, id ASC)` — backdated receipts can land ahead of existing layers (e.g. invoice arrives late), and ties broken deterministically by id (verified by `test_ties_broken_by_id_when_received_at_identical` using `freezegun` to force the timestamp tie). The composite `ix_cost_layers_item_received` covers the ORDER BY. **`current_qty` ownership**: chosen "engine owns it" over "route owns it". The alternative invites every M2/M3/M4 route to redo the same arithmetic and risk drift. The engine is the only place that can compute `total_cost` correctly (FIFO sum), so co-locating `current_qty` mutation makes the inventory-level invariant atomic with the cost-level one. The I3 self-critique entry "current_qty not updated when units are created or archived" is now fixable — the M2 route for unique-tracked stock-in will go through the engine and bump `current_qty`. The historical wart (existing unique items show 0 until a movement fires) is still present; a one-shot backfill is M2's call. **No audit-log writes inside the engine**: that's the route's responsibility. The engine is below the audit layer. **No route-level integration in M1**: M2-M6 each add a route that wraps the engine. **Tests**: 44 new (15 in `tests/unit/test_cost_models.py` covering defaults + enum round-trips + FK NOT NULLs + qty_remaining-vs-qty_received independence + plain-Integer po_id/stock_take_id; 29 in `tests/unit/test_cost_engine.py` covering: receipt 9 (correct fields, current_qty increment, total_cost set, received_at default + override, qty/unit_cost validation matrix incl. zero-cost-allowed, unflushed-movement-rejected); single-layer consume 2 (partial + exact); multi-layer consume 3 (FIFO across two layers, exhausted-layer skipped, id-tiebreak with frozen time); errors 6 (over-consume raises with carried-fields, atomic-on-raise, no-layers-at-all, zero qty, negative qty, unflushed movement); isolation 1 (sibling items don't cross-consume); open_value 6 (empty, single, multi-source-sum, exhausted-excluded, partial-included, isolation); combined 2 (full receipt→consume→receipt→consume cycle + positive→negative adjustment cycle). 620 unit+integration (was 576, +44). 9 e2e unchanged. ruff + mypy clean (16 source files; +1 — `app/cost_engine.py`). Migration applies upgrade + downgrade cleanly against a fresh SQLite DB. |

The first stock-in movement (M1+) will own this column. **Audit vocabulary**: `item.{created,updated,archived,unarchived}`. Created `after_json` carries every stored field incl. `current_qty`. Updates use the sparse `_diff` pattern. **Templates**: new `items_list.html` (active/archived tabs + columns + per-row archive/unarchive forms with CSRF) and `items_form.html` (12 fields incl. category `<select>` with disabled "group label" options for non-leaf top-levels + active leaves only, supplier/location `<select>` with blank "— none —" + active rows only, tracking-mode `<select>`, `requires_checkout` checkbox, decimal inputs as `inputmode="decimal"`, read-only `current_qty` display visible only on edit). `base.html` updated: new "Items" nav link visible to Manager + Admin (data-testid `nav-items`, `aria-current` on `/admin/items*`). 64 new tests (`tests/unit/test_items.py` 9: model defaults + decimal round-trip + unique-tracking-mode + sku-uniqueness-spans-archived + qr-uniqueness-when-set + qr-NULL-coexists + qr-uniqueness-spans-archived + taxonomy_node_id required;
