---

## Self-critique notes (rolling)

*(Carry forward weaknesses noted during iteration self-critiques but not yet addressed. Clear an entry when it gets fixed in a later slice. Don't let this get longer than ~10 items — if it does, something has gone off the rails.)*

- **I1c / one URL, two postures.** `/admin/items/{id}/edit` serves both an editable form (Manager + Office + Admin) and a read-only view (Workshop). The "Edit" / "View" link-label split makes it honest from the list page, but a sysadmin reviewing access logs would see Workshop hitting an `/edit` URL and might briefly worry. A cleaner shape would be a separate `/admin/items/{id}/view` route specifically for read-only — same template, different role gate, same URL semantics from the linker's POV. Defer unless a real user finds the dual-purpose URL confusing.
- **I1c / `disabled` inputs vs proper read-only fields.** Workshop sees a form-shaped UI where every input is greyed out. Browser-level `disabled` is keyboard-skippable + screen-reader-announced as "disabled", but it still looks like a form. A more accessible shape would be a definition list (`<dl>`) with the values as plain text — the field labels are the same, the values render as `<dd>{{ form.sku }}</dd>` etc. Probably worth doing in P2 (accessibility pass), where the wider concern is "does the rendered surface match its semantic role". Cost is a second template (or a big template branch) — defer until P2 lands.
- **I1c / Workshop has no read access to item-units (`/admin/items/{id}/units`).** Inherits the existing M2 / M3 / M4 gap. For unique-tracked items, Workshop can't see *which* physical units exist — only the aggregate view (the `tracking_mode = unique` flag is visible on the read-only edit form but the unit list isn't reachable). Stays a Manager + Office surface only. Will revisit when SC1's scan-mode lands and a Workshop user genuinely needs to identify a specific unit by serial.
- **I1c / `_can_save_item` echoes a role-list that already lives on the POST route's `require_role`.** The predicate is True for Manager + Office + Admin; the POST routes use `require_role(MANAGER, OFFICE)` (and Admin bypasses). If a future role gets POST access (or is removed), both spots have to move in lockstep. One-line predicate, hard to forget — but worth flagging. The same pattern already exists for `_can_edit_thresholds` (Manager + Admin) so this isn't a new shape.
- **I1c / no negative-path e2e walk for Workshop POST 403s.** Workshop's POST 403s on items are integration-tested but not e2e. Same gap the I3a self-critique already documents for items / suppliers / locations / taxonomy. A "settings UX polish" slice should add a single e2e that proves a Workshop user submitting a tampered POST gets a 403 page. Cheap; defer.
- **M6 / Workshop sees per-layer unit_cost and per-movement total_cost on the detail page.** The cost-layers table renders `unit_cost` for every open layer; the timeline renders `total_cost` per movement. Workshop is allowed on the page (mirrors M2/M3/M4 form surfaces, which already show the same values). MISSION §3 says Workshop "Cannot see aggregated cost data or reports" — strict reading argues per-item cost data is too generous. Counter-reading: per-item is not aggregation (a single item's history), and the M2/M3/M4 forms already commit us to this exposure. Documenting; flag for clarification once a real Workshop user gives feedback. Cheapest restrictive change if needed: a `_can_see_cost(user)` predicate that hides the cost columns + open_value summary for Workshop.
- **M6 / out-of-range `?page=N` clamps silently to `[1, page_count]`.** Stale links (a user bookmarks page 5, more movements come in or get archived, page count drops) land on the closest valid page without an error. Friendlier than 400, less surprising than 500. Tested both directions (`?page=99` clamps to last; `?page=0` clamps to first). If a future debugging session needs to know the user "asked for" page 99, the request log captures that. Document.
- **M6 / pagination is forward-only (prev / next), no first / last / jump-to-page.** For an item with hundreds of pages of movements (high-velocity consumable received daily for years), navigating to the middle is tedious. Acceptable for v1 scale (no real item has 100+ movements yet). Defer to a polish slice once a real item's timeline hits the threshold; the cheap add is `?page=1` and `?page={page_count}` links + a select-dropdown.
- **M6 / `_attach_directions_and_breakdown` does two extra queries per page.** One for the "is there a layer with `source_movement_id` in this page" check (gives the `+` set), one for the consumption-rows-with-their-parent-layer's-received_at (gives the `-` set + the breakdown). Could be collapsed into a single LEFT-OUTER-JOIN query but the two-query shape reads cleanly and runs in <1ms at v1 scale. Documenting; reconsider when profiling shows a problem.
- **M6 / TRANSFER (M5) direction defensive `else` branch.** A movement with neither a layer nor a consumption renders with `direction = ""` and the qty column shows just the qty (no sign). M5's TRANSFER will be the first writer that produces such a row. The page won't crash; it just won't say "transfer to location X" for now. M5's job to add a transfer-specific render branch (probably an arrow + locations).
- **M6 / layer-breakdown `<tr>` uses hard-coded `colspan=6`.** If a future column is added to the timeline table (e.g. a "Note" column), the colspan baseline shifts and the breakdown sub-row falls out of alignment. One-line fix when it happens; document the maintenance hazard now.
- ~~**M6 / Detail link from the items list isn't reachable by Workshop.**~~ *Resolved in I1c: Workshop now has GET access to `/admin/items` and the per-row "Details" + "View" links work for them.*
- **M6 / no audit on read.** Read surface; consistent with the rest of the app (the audit log captures state changes, not lookups). Flag only if a future "who looked at item X" capability is needed (probably not in v1).
- ~~**M4 / `MovementType.adjustment` row in the recent-movements table doesn't expose direction.**~~ *Resolved in M6 (for the canonical view): the item-detail page's timeline computes the sign from the linked layer/consumption rows (`_attach_directions_and_breakdown`) and renders qty as `+20` / `-15` via the `data-direction` attribute + the prefix on `timeline-qty`. The form-side recent-movements lists on M2/M3/M4 still show unsigned qty — those serve "did my last action land?" feedback, not a forensic audit; the detail page is the canonical view.*
- **M4 / direction is encoded in audit but not on the movement row itself.** `stock_movements` has no `direction` column — for ADJUSTMENT rows, the direction is derivable from the existence of a `cost_layers.source_movement_id == movement.id` row (increase) vs a `cost_layer_consumptions.movement_id == movement.id` row (decrease). The audit shape duplicates that derivation as a convenience for the audit-viewer (M6 / R-series). Adding a `direction` column to `stock_movements` would create a redundant source of truth — the layer/consumption tables are already definitive. Document; flag if the M6 timeline render pays a visible cost in joins.
- **M4 / `unit_cost` is always rendered but only required for increases.** The form has the field with an explanatory `<em>required for increases; ignored for decreases</em>` line, and the integration test `test_unit_cost_ignored_on_decrease` confirms garbage in that field is accepted on decreases. A user could reasonably submit a decrease with a typed unit_cost expecting it to be recorded — they'd get a successful 303 with no error and no record of their typing. Today the cost engine's contract ("consume price comes from layers") makes this the right thing, but the UX is silent about it. Fix shape (deferred): HTMX swap to hide the field when direction=decrease — would also be the first concrete HTMX use case (the library's been loaded since F4 + unused). Don't fix until a second HTMX use case exists.
- **M4 / `unit_cost_decimal: Decimal | None` requires an `assert ... is not None` for mypy narrowing.** The variable is set on the `direction == "increase"` branch only; the call to `record_receipt` lives inside the same branch but mypy doesn't narrow across the assignment + branch boundary. The assert is one line + a comment. Could be eliminated by inlining the parse inside the branch, but that re-issues the helper call with the same kwargs. Acceptable noise. Document.
- **M4 / two parallel audit-after dicts (one per direction).** The increase + decrease branches each construct their own `audit_after` dict with overlapping but distinct keys. A future refactor could compute a base dict and conditionally extend it (`if direction == "increase": audit_after.update(...)`), but the two-dict shape reads top-to-bottom and the test surface verifies each shape independently. Acceptable; flag if a third dispatch case appears (it won't — `MovementType` has IN / OUT / ADJUSTMENT / TRANSFER and TRANSFER is M5's no-cost-change move).
- **M4 / no `item_unit_id` linkage for unique-tracked items.** Inherits M2 / M3 gap. Defer to a focused slice once the qty-tracked path settles.
- **M4 / no backdated `received_at` UI on increase / no backdated `created_at` UI overall.** Inherits M2 / M3 gap. Same fix shape; same deferred reasoning.
- ~~**M4 / pagination on the recent-movements list is still hard-coded `LIMIT 10`.**~~ *Partially resolved in M6: the detail page introduces proper pagination (`?page=N&page_size=20`). The form-side recent-movements lists (M2 / M3 / M4) still cap at LIMIT 10 — those serve "did my last action land?" feedback, not a forensic timeline. The canonical full-history view now lives on `/detail`.*
- **M4 / no `record_audit` on insufficient-stock decrease failure.** Same as M3 — failed write isn't a state change, so no audit. Documented in M3 entry; same logic applies.
- **M4 / four forms now share the "in-form errors" carve-out asymmetry.** The error-rendering form-rerender pattern that M3 introduced for stock-out (insufficient stock) now also applies to M4's adjust on the decrease leg. Every other 400 in M4's POST (blank qty, blank direction, blank reason, blank unit_cost on increase, archived item, etc.) still lands on FastAPI's bare exception page. Six other forms across the app share the same gap. The "settings UX polish" slice should extend the M3/M4 in-form-errors shape across all of them; cost-of-fix grows linearly with each new form.
- **M3 / "in-form errors" carve-out is asymmetric.** Insufficient-stock 400 re-renders the form with the user's inputs preserved + an `<p data-testid="stock-out-error">` block; every other 400 in the route (blank qty, zero / negative / non-numeric qty, archived item) lands on FastAPI's bare exception page — same as the rest of the seven-form running tally. Justified for the data-dependent failure (the qty isn't a typo; the warehouse changed under the user), but creates two visually distinct error UIs in one route. Self-critique: when the long-pending "settings UX polish" slice lands, this carve-out should drive the polish — it's the only place in the codebase where the *right* error UI already exists, so the polish slice's job is to extend the same shape (preserved inputs + error block) to the other six forms (suppliers / locations / taxonomy / field-defs / items / item-units / stock-in / stock-out's other 400 paths).
- **M3 / `db.rollback()` on insufficient-stock relies on engine atomicity.** The route's rollback is *only* dropping the orphan `StockMovement` we added before the engine call — `consume_fifo` itself never mutated anything when it raises (M1's atomic-on-raise contract, tested by `test_over_consumption_is_atomic`). If a future engine refactor breaks that contract (e.g. adds an early write before the available-qty check), the route's rollback would silently mask the partial state. The integration test `test_consume_more_than_open_layers_returns_400_with_form` asserts `layer.qty_remaining == Decimal("3")` and `item.current_qty == Decimal("3")` after the failed POST, so a regression would fail that test loudly. Acceptable belt-and-braces; document the dependency.
- **M3 / route reloads `item` after rollback.** After `db.rollback()`, the original `item` reference is in a detached/expired state (SQLAlchemy semantics). The route calls `_get_item_or_404(db, item_id)` to reload before re-rendering. A subtle alternative would be `db.refresh(item)` — but `refresh` on a rolled-back instance also requires a re-fetch and produces no measurable difference. The reload is more obvious about intent. Document; no action needed.
- **M3 / `total_cost` audit string carries column-quantised scale.** When the engine reads `layer.unit_cost` back from `Numeric(14, 4)` storage and computes `take * layer.unit_cost`, the product carries scale 4 (e.g. `Decimal("8.0000")`). The audit row's `after_json["total_cost"]` is `str(...)` of that, so it serialises as `"8.0000"` not `"8"`. M2's stock-in audit shows `"5.00"` instead because the unit_cost there is the route's fresh input (not round-tripped through DB). Tests pin this behaviour explicitly (`assert row.after_json["total_cost"] == "8.0000"`). Inconsistent string scale across IN vs OUT audits — but the *Decimal* values are equal under value-comparison, and the stored representation is durable. If a downstream report ever string-matches on these (it shouldn't — it should `Decimal()` them), the wart bites. Document; flag for any audit-viewer / report slice.
- **M3 / no `item_unit_id` linkage for unique-tracked items.** Inherits M2's gap. A workshop user consuming a unique-tracked tool today records a quantity-based out movement that decrements `current_qty` (which is itself wrong-by-current-design for unique-tracked items, see I3 self-critique entry); the consumed unit is not identified. For the typical "bulk consumable" stock-out (raw materials, polish), this is fine; for unique items it's wrong. Probable fix: a unit picker on the form when the item is unique-tracked. Defer to a focused slice once M4 / M5 settle the qty-tracked path.
- **M3 / no backdated `created_at` UI.** The route always uses `datetime.now(UTC)`. Same gap as M2; same fix shape (a "happened at" date input on the form). The cost engine's FIFO order doesn't depend on `created_at` for OUT movements (it only walks layers in `received_at` order), so a backdated OUT in the engine sense is meaningless — but for *audit* purposes ("we forgot to record this consumption from last Tuesday"), the route should record the actual time. PO5 / M4 will both want this; defer.
- **M3 / no `record_audit` on insufficient-stock failure.** A failed stock-out attempt isn't audit-logged: the `db.rollback()` discards the orphan movement, the route returns 400 with the error block, no audit row written. MISSION §3 says "every state-changing action records an audit row" — a failed write isn't a state change, so this is consistent with the existing convention (other 400s also don't audit). But for *forensics* purposes ("did anyone try to consume 1000 units of X today?"), the absence of a record is a gap. Consistent with M2's behaviour for failed receipts (no audit on `qty=-1` etc.). Document; defer until a real fraud-detection requirement appears.
- ~~**M3 / pagination on the recent-movements list is still hard-coded `LIMIT 10`.**~~ *Resolved in M6: the detail page's timeline is now properly paginated (`?page=N&page_size=20`). The form-side LIMIT 10 stands by design.*
- **M3 / `_render_stock_out_form` takes 7 named kwargs.** The signature is verbose because the GET handler and the error path both need to render the same template. An alternative would be passing a context dict directly, but the kwargs make the call sites self-documenting. Acceptable; flag if a third caller arrives.
- ~~**M3 / no per-OUT layer breakdown in the recent-movements table.**~~ *Resolved in M6: the detail page's timeline renders per-row `layer-breakdown` blocks for OUT and negative-adjustment movements showing each consumed layer (qty_consumed × unit_cost_at_consumption + layer received_at). The form-side recent-movements list still doesn't show the breakdown, but that's by design (the detail page is the canonical full-history view).*
- **M3 / OUT reason is optional.** The route accepts a blank reason; M4's adjustment movements will require it (variance has to be attributed). For OUT, "the workshop consumed it for production" is the implicit default; freeing the user from typing that every time matches the "workshop staff aren't technical" NFR. If a manager later wants reason-required-for-out (audit-trail polish), it's a one-line change in `_parse_positive_decimal`-adjacent validation. Document, don't change the contract.
- ~~**M2 / Workshop has no UI path to find an item to stock-in.**~~ *Resolved in I1c: Workshop now has GET access to `/admin/items` (read-only list) and `/admin/items/{id}/edit` (read-only form with the in/out/adjust action links visible). The fallback path (browse → click View → click Stock-in) is in place. SC1's scan flow remains the primary Workshop entry point.*
- **M2 / no `item_unit_id` linkage for unique-tracked items.** The route accepts any item (qty- or unique-tracked) and records a quantity-based receipt that bumps `item.current_qty` and creates a single cost layer. For a unique-tracked item, the receipt doesn't say *which* physical unit was received — `stock_movements.item_unit_id` is left NULL even though MISSION §6 lists it. Consequence: a workshop user receiving a new tool today can record the receipt + cost but the resulting layer isn't tied to the specific `item_unit` row created in I3. Adequate for v1's qty-tracked dominant case (raw materials, consumables); for unique-tracked items the receipt-vs-unit linkage is a known gap. Probable fix: a unit picker on the form when the item is unique-tracked, populated from the active+available units. Defer to a focused slice once M3-M4 settle the qty-tracked path.
- **M2 / no `received_at` UI control.** The route always uses `datetime.now(UTC)`. The engine supports backdating (M1 explicitly tested it via `freezegun`) but no form input surfaces it. For invoices that arrive a week after physical receipt — common in workshops — the FIFO order will be insert-order, not actual-receipt-order. Acceptable for v1's manual workflow; PO5 / M4 will both want a backdated receipt UI and that's the right time to add the input. Document.
- **M2 / form re-renders empty after a successful submit.** A workshop user doing five receipts at the same unit cost has to type the cost five times. Retaining the most recent unit_cost (or qty) in the form on the post-redirect GET would shave time off bulk receipts. Not a UX disaster — the form is short — but a probable polish slice. Defer.
- **M2 / no in-form error rendering (sixth form with the gap).** Validation 400s land on the bare FastAPI exception page, same as the rest of the settings forms. The running tally of forms missing in-form error rendering is now: suppliers / locations / taxonomy / field-defs / items / item-units / stock-in = seven. The cost of fixing each one in isolation is no different from fixing them together. Note for the still-pending "settings UX polish" slice.
- **M2 / no DB-level immutability on `stock_movements`.** The route never UPDATEs or DELETEs movements; the engine sets `total_cost` exactly once and never touches the column again. But there's no DB trigger enforcing it. Same posture as M1's flag — partial-trigger ("reject UPDATE on every column except `total_cost`") is awkward in SQLite + would need separate Postgres expression. Defer until a "data correction" path is concretely needed.
- **M2 / `record_receipt` raises `ValueError` for engine-internal violations.** The route's pre-validation catches `qty <= 0` and `unit_cost < 0` before the engine ever sees them, so the engine's `ValueError` paths are dead in M2's call path. Defense-in-depth. If a future caller bypasses the pre-validation (a test, a PO5 path that takes engine inputs from a different source), the engine still defends. Documented in M1's self-critique entry on engine input shape. No action.
- ~~**M2 / pagination on the recent-movements list.**~~ *Resolved in M6 (for the canonical view): the detail page's timeline now paginates. Form-side LIMIT 10 by design.*
- **M2 / route-pattern collisions across `/admin/items/...`.** `app/items.py`, `app/item_units.py`, and `app/movements.py` all mount under `/admin/items`. Path templates in use: `/admin/items` (list), `/admin/items/new` (form), `/admin/items/{item_id}/edit` (edit form), `/admin/items/{item_id}` (POST update), `/admin/items/{item_id}/archive`, `/admin/items/{item_id}/unarchive`, `/admin/items/{item_id}/in` (M2 GET + POST), `/admin/items/{item_id}/units` (list), `/admin/items/{item_id}/units/new`, `/admin/items/{item_id}/units` (POST), `/admin/items/units/{unit_id}/edit`, `/admin/items/units/{unit_id}` (POST), `/admin/items/units/{unit_id}/{archive,unarchive}`. M2's two new routes (`{id}/in`) don't collide with anything. The existing I3 wart (a future flat-by-id unit POST would clash with `POST /admin/items/{item_id}` from items.py) hasn't gotten worse with M2. Document; same rename plan applies if it ever bites.
- **M2 / no cross-item recent-movements view.** The dashboard slice (R1+) will want a "recent activity" view across all items. Today the recent-movements query is per-item and lives in `app/movements.py::_recent_movements`. When R1 lands, the cross-item version will share the same `select(StockMovement, User.email).outerjoin(...)` shape — extract then. Acceptable today.
- **M1 / no FK constraints on `stock_movements.po_id` / `stock_take_id`.** They're plain `Integer NULL` columns in M1 because the `purchase_orders` and `stock_takes` tables don't exist yet. A direct INSERT with `po_id = 999_999` succeeds today (verified by `test_po_and_stock_take_ids_are_plain_integers` — the test exists to *document* the gap, not endorse it). PO2 / ST1 must add the FK constraint as part of their migration. If those slices forget, the route layer will be the only thing keeping the column honest, and a future buggy code path could write garbage. Cheap to fix when the time comes; the column is already nullable so the FK addition is non-breaking.
- **M1 / no DB-level immutability triggers on the cost tables.** The audit-log triggers (which reject UPDATE/DELETE on `audit_log`) are not extended to `cost_layers`, `cost_layer_consumptions`, or `stock_movements`. The engine is the only writer and never UPDATEs `qty_received` / `unit_cost` / `received_at` / `source` (only `qty_remaining`), and never DELETEs anything. But this is route-discipline-only: a misbehaving migration script or an admin running raw SQL could corrupt history. Re-evaluate when a "data correction" UI ever lands; a partial trigger ("reject UPDATE on every column except `qty_remaining`") is awkward in SQLite (CHECK on OLD/NEW row diff) and would need to be expressed differently in Postgres. Defer until concretely needed.
- **M1 / engine takes a flushed `StockMovement` rather than constructing one.** The contract is documented in `app/cost_engine.py`'s module docstring and enforced with a `movement.id is None` raise. Caller boilerplate every route handler will write: `db.add(movement); db.flush(); record_receipt(db, ..., movement=movement)`. A small `with_movement(db, item, type, qty, ..., make_layer_or_consume)` helper would tidy that up — flag for after M2 + M3 land and the duplication is concrete.
- **M1 / FIFO assumes `received_at` is a meaningful column.** Layers carry the timestamp the *receipt* happened, not the wall-clock time the row was inserted. `record_receipt(received_at=None)` defaults to `datetime.now(UTC)`, which is fine for a synchronous receipt. A backdated receipt (invoice arrives a week late, operator wants the layer to land at the historical date) requires the route to compute and pass `received_at`. M2's UI must surface a "received date" field that defaults to today but is editable; without it, all manual stock-ins land at "now" and the FIFO order is purely insert-order, which is also fine — but the engine supports the richer behaviour now, ahead of the UI catching up. Document.
- **M1 / `consume_fifo` loads all open layers in memory.** Items with thousands of layers (e.g. a high-velocity consumable received daily for a year) would load 365+ rows just to consume from the first one. SQLite is fast enough that this is invisible at v1 scale, but for a scaled deployment a `.limit(1)` per iteration plus a running `qty_remaining` check would be cheaper. Defer; flag for the P3 Postgres-parity slice if profiling shows it.
- **M1 / no per-engine-call transaction boundary.** The engine uses `db.flush()` but never commits or rolls back. The route layer is responsible for committing on success and rolling back on any exception (including the `InsufficientStockError` path — though that path mutates nothing, so a rollback is a no-op). FastAPI's request-scoped session lifecycle handles this for HTTP routes (the dependency wraps the request in a transaction); a bg job calling the engine directly must handle its own transaction. Documented in the module docstring.
- **M1 / `total_cost` is `Numeric(14, 4)` but products of two `Numeric(14, 4)` operands can exceed that scale.** Decimal multiplication preserves both scales (4 + 4 = 8 fractional digits at most). The engine relies on the column type to round on write. For most realistic costs the product is well within range, but a pathological `0.0001 × 0.0001 × 1e10` could in theory be lossy on the way to the column. Flag for a hardening pass; concrete fix would be `Numeric(28, 8)` for `total_cost`. Not urgent.
- **M1 / no e2e walk for the engine.** Pure-logic slice with no route surface, so no Playwright walk added. M2 will be the first to exercise the engine through a route, and that walk should verify the *cost* outcome (not just "qty went up") — at minimum, after a stock-in, a value column on the item list should reflect the new total. Note for M2 to wire that into the e2e walk, not skip it.
- **I3 / `current_qty` is not updated when units are created or archived.** For a unique-tracked item with N active+available units, the items list still shows `current_qty = 0` (the I1a "current_qty is read-only via the route" rule). The honest count is `COUNT(units WHERE archived_at IS NULL AND status = 'available')`. Today no UI consumes `current_qty` for a decision (no reorder dashboard, no low-stock alert), so the wart is invisible to users — but the moment **PO1** lands, unique items would never trigger reorder. The fix is M1's job: when the FIFO movement engine lands, unit creation should emit an `in` movement that bumps `current_qty` (and creates a cost layer); unit archive should emit an `out`. Don't shim a recompute in I3; the M1 plumbing is already going to need to own this column.
- **I3 / `status` enum has only `available` + `lost` — `checked_out` is deferred to C-series.** A future status-list expansion is a Python-only change (column is `String(16)` storing the enum value, no migration needed). Decision: don't over-reserve — `available` and `lost` are real workshop states; `checked_out` will be derived from an open `checkouts` row when C2 lands. If a future need wants a third "in repair" state, it's a one-line enum addition.
- **I3 / no cascading archive: archiving an item leaves its units active.** A manager who archives a unique-tracked item still sees its units on `/admin/items/{id}/units?show=active`. Same posture as taxonomy (S4): silently archiving the children of a parent is a data-integrity risk we'd rather make explicit. The list view shows an "archived" note + hides the New CTA, so the workflow is "archive each unit, then archive the item" if the manager wants a clean cleanup. Acceptable for v1; revisit when checkout history (C-series) lands and a half-archived state becomes painful.
- **I3 / tracking-mode flip after units exist is silent.** A manager can edit a unique-tracked item with units and set `tracking_mode = qty`. The unit rows stay (per "existing items keep their stored values") but become invisible-by-default (the units list still renders them, but with a "qty-tracked" note + hidden New CTA). Flipping back to `unique` shows them again. No data loss; no defensive 400. If a future user complains that flipping should warn or block, route-level guard is a 5-line addition. Document, don't fix.
- **I3 / `_resolve_optional_location` and `_location_options` are duplicated between `app/items.py` and `app/item_units.py`.** Two callers, identical contract (archived-FK preservation via `current_id`). Same trade-off as `_is_leaf` (duplicated between `app/items.py` and `app/field_defs.py`). Extracting to a shared module would force a third file (`app/_settings_helpers.py`?) and a cross-module dependency for a 30-line helper. Acceptable today; extract on the third caller.
- **I3 / no pagination on the units list.** A unique-tracked tool catalogue might have hundreds of physical units. Same wart as the items list; same fix shape (`?page=N&page_size=50`). Don't ship I1c without it. Probable order: pagination lands as a single sweep across items + units + audit-viewer when M6 needs the timeline view.
- **I3 / no e2e walk for the role-based 403 on units.** Workshop / Office / Pending negative paths are integration-tested but not e2e. Same gap as items / suppliers / locations / taxonomy. A "settings UX polish" slice should add a single e2e that proves a Workshop user hitting `/admin/items/.../units` gets a 403 page. Cheap; defer.
- **I3 / `status` is rendered as the raw enum value** (`available` / `lost`) in the units list. Workshop staff don't need that vocabulary; "Available" / "Lost" with a coloured pill would be friendlier. Cosmetic; defer to a UI polish slice.
- **I3 / no per-unit notes column.** MISSION §3 mentions "condition note" on a checkout (C-series) but there's no free-text note on the unit row itself. If a manager wants to record "this mould has a small chip but is still usable", today's only option is a status flip to `lost` (overloaded) or off-system notes. Schema sketch in §6 doesn't list a notes column — flag as a possible scope expansion if real users hit it.
- **I3 / 14 endpoints under `/admin/items/...` across two routers.** `app/items.py` has 7 (`/`, `/new`, `/{id}/edit`, `/{id}` POST, `/{id}/{archive,unarchive}`); `app/item_units.py` has 7 (`/{item_id}/units[?...]`, `/{item_id}/units/new`, `/{item_id}/units` POST, `/units/{unit_id}/edit`, `/units/{unit_id}` POST, `/units/{unit_id}/{archive,unarchive}`). Path collisions are *avoided* by segment count (item routes use 0–2 segments after `/admin/items/`; unit routes use 2–3). A future refactor that adds a 1-segment unit-flat route would clash with the items.py `POST /admin/items/{item_id}` 1-segment route. Document; if it happens, the cheap fix is renaming `/admin/items/units/...` → `/admin/units/...`.
- ~~**I3 / DoD #2 is essentially complete but unticked.**~~ *Resolved in I3a (iteration 16): `test_admin_creates_qty_then_unique_item_end_to_end` added to `tests/e2e/test_items_e2e.py`. DoD #2 is now ticked, backed by ~100 integration tests AND two e2e walks (manager + admin).*
- **I3a / two e2e walks share the session DB and a definition-order cleanup contract.** The manager walk archives "Items E2E Cat" + "RM-E2E-001" in cleanup so the admin walk starts with empty active lists; the admin walk archives "Admin Items E2E Cat" + "AD-E2E-001" + "AD-SN-001" so downstream files (`test_locations_e2e.py`, `test_suppliers_e2e.py`, `test_taxonomy_e2e.py`) start with empty active lists too. Pytest runs the two walks in definition order (manager first, admin second) — if a future refactor reorders them or splits across files, the cleanup chain breaks subtly. Today's mitigation: each walk uses unique names so reordering causes loud failures (`expect(items-empty).to_be_visible()` in the admin walk would fail if the manager walk hadn't run first to clean up). Acceptable for v1; if a third walk lands, factor cleanup into a Playwright fixture rather than per-test cleanup steps.
- **I3a / no Workshop / Office negative-path e2e walk.** The admin walk proves a positive role path; the existing manager walk proves another. Workshop=403 / Office=403 / pending=403 are integration-tested across every router but no e2e walk renders the actual 403 page for those roles. DoD #9 wants both. Cheap to add (one short walk per negative role) but premature today — the e2e suite is up to 9 walks and adding three more without M-series progress would unbalance the suite. Defer until I1c (Workshop read-only) lands and the Workshop walk gets a positive path to pair with.
- **I2 / two-step UX for items in categories with required custom fields.** The unfiltered `New item` CTA goes to `/admin/items/new` with no `?node_id=`, so the form renders core fields + a free category dropdown but no custom-field inputs. If the user picks a category that has required defs and submits, they get a bare 400 ("Alloy is required"). Workaround: deep-link via `/admin/items/new?node_id=X` (as the e2e walk does). The clean fix is HTMX-swap the custom-field section when the category dropdown changes — first concrete use case for the HTMX library that's been loaded since F4 but unused. Probably worth a small focused slice (call it I2.1) once a *second* HTMX use case appears (so the pattern lands with two examples instead of one). Don't fix in isolation.
- **I2 / required-flag for boolean = "must be checked".** Documented in the `app/items.py` module docstring and the route logic (`fd.required` + `value is not True` → 400). Conservative interpretation; matches "I confirm the T&Cs" patterns. If a future user complains that "required" should mean "user must explicitly answer one way or the other" (i.e. tri-state needed), the schema doesn't cover it. Note for S6 if it comes up; for v1 the documented semantics stand.
- **I2 / select stores the chosen option as plain text, not a stable id.** Same as the S5 self-critique entry already in this list. If the manager renames an option in the def's `options_json`, existing `value_text` rows still hold the old string and won't round-trip through the form (will fail the "value in options" check on next edit). MISSION §3 "existing items keep their stored values" applies: keep the old string. The cheapest backwards-compatible fix when this matters is a value-vs-label split in `options_json`, e.g. `[{"value": "9", "label": "9 carat"}, ...]` — schema is already JSON, no migration needed. Defer until a real complaint.
- **I2 / archived field defs are invisible on edit, including their values.** The form skips archived defs entirely — values stay on the item but the user editing can't see they exist. For a manager debugging a historical item, the audit log is the only path. Acceptable for v1; the M6 item-detail page should surface "historical fields" as a read-only section. Defer.
- **I2 / category change on edit doesn't migrate / clear values for fields no longer in the new schema.** If an item moves from leaf A to leaf B, A's defs no longer apply but rows for them still exist on the item. Those rows are invisible (form looks at B's defs only) and won't round-trip if the item ever moves back. Stretch reading of MISSION §3 — "existing items keep their stored values" arguably implies "even after re-categorisation". Conservative for v1; consider an audit-only "category change cleared field foo" entry in S6.
- **I2 / type-change on a field def is still silent (S5-flagged, now actively load-bearing).** When items reference a def by id and a manager flips the def's `type` from `text` → `number`, the existing `value_text` rows are now wrong relative to the schema. The edit form would render the old string in a `number` input, fail HTML validation, and the parse would 400. We don't migrate or warn. Concrete S6 work now that I2 has shipped — was theoretical before.
- **I2 / `_parse_custom_field` raises `HTTPException(400)` directly on bad input.** Mirrors the rest of `app/items.py` (the FK / decimal / leaf resolvers all 400 directly). Makes "render form with errors keyed by field" harder later — the route would need to catch each HTTPException and stash it. The "settings UX polish" slice that's in the long-running self-critique list is now responsible for *six* forms, not five — it should refactor to a shared `(value, error_or_None)` shape across all of them in a single pass.
- **I2 / no in-form error rendering on items either** (sixth form with the gap, per the running tally). When the I2 slice lands the polish, it'll be the cheapest moment — most of the validation logic is already concentrated in `_normalise` + `_collect_custom_fields`. Cost-of-fix grows linearly with each new form; don't ship I3 without considering whether to roll the whole thing.
- **I2 / `_collect_custom_fields` requires a sync-friendly `FormData` interface.** Type-checks `form.getlist(...)` and `form.get(...)` — the `# type: ignore[arg-type]` on `getlist` is because mypy thinks `FormData.getlist` is `list[Any]` not `list[str]`, but at runtime any value coming out of an HTML form is a string. Defensible; could be tightened by branching on `isinstance(v, str)` per entry, but cosmetic noise.
- ~~**I1a / archived-FK on item edit silently drops the link.**~~ *Resolved in I1b: option (a) chosen — include the currently-assigned archived row in the dropdown with "(archived)" suffix; resolvers now accept an unchanged archived FK and reject *switches to* archived FKs. Tested in `TestArchivedFKPreservation` (12 tests).*
- **I1b / threshold restriction is silent (override) not visible (disabled input).** When Office submits new `reorder_threshold` / `reorder_qty` values, the route silently overrides them with the existing row's values *before* validation. A 400 would be more informative but would also leak the field shape (and force the form to include disabled fields whose values matter for re-submission). Silent override matches the existing `current_qty` pattern — that field is also never settable through the form. The wart: an Office user manually constructing a tampered request gets a 303 with no error, and might not realise their change was discarded. Acceptable for v1: the form template hides those inputs from Office, so legitimate UIs never produce that submission. If a future audit-viewer UI lands and shows "no diff" rows for what looks like a successful Office edit, surfacing a flash message ("threshold change ignored — Manager-only") would be the cheap fix.
- **I1b / `_can_edit_thresholds` checks role explicitly, doesn't fit FastAPI's dependency model.** FastAPI dependencies gate route entry, not field-level write permissions. The current shape — `require_role(MANAGER, OFFICE)` admits both, then the handler explicitly checks `user.role in (MANAGER, ADMIN)` to decide whether to honour the threshold fields — is the right boring solution; building a "field-level dependency" framework would over-engineer a single field pair. If a third Office-restricted field appears (likely candidates: cost-related fields once M1 lands), tabulate the rules in a small `_OFFICE_RESTRICTED_FIELDS` set and apply them in a loop. Don't extract before the second field arrives.
- **I1b / archived-FK preservation only kicks in for the assigned row.** The form lists active rows + the *current* assignment if archived. An item that previously had supplier A (now archived) and was edited to clear it, then later gets opened again — the Manager can no longer pick A back, only blank or active suppliers. That's correct: re-assigning to an archived supplier is a *new* association with archived data, which we don't allow (per the same rule as creating new items under archived categories). If a manager wants to bring A back, they unarchive A first — that's the right workflow. Document if a future user complains, but don't relax the rule.
- **I1a / no pagination on the items list.** Same gap as suppliers/locations/taxonomy, but items hit the NFR threshold (`5,000 items load in <1s`) much sooner — UC has thousands of potential items vs tens of suppliers. Today the list page renders every active or archived row inline. Not blocking I1a (zero rows in tests, hundreds tolerable in prod), but the next slice that touches the items list (M6 item-detail timeline, R5 CSV export, a dedicated polish slice) must land pagination. Don't ship I1b without it. Probable shape: `?page=N&page_size=50`, with `previous`/`next` links + a per-row count in the header.
- **I1a / `_is_leaf` is now duplicated between `app/items.py` and `app/field_defs.py`.** Two callers, one-line predicate, both must move in lockstep if the leaf rule changes. Acceptable today — extraction would force a third file and a cross-module dependency for a four-line function. Extract on the third caller (likely SC1 scan-mode page if it filters by leaf, or a future "items by category" report).
- **I1a / category `<select>` uses disabled `<option>` elements as group headers, not proper `<optgroup>`.** Disabled options work and are announced by screen readers as "disabled, [text]" — but `<optgroup label="…">` is the right HTML for "this is a header, the items inside are picks". A future accessibility-polish slice should swap. Cosmetic; not blocking the DoD or any NFR.
- **I1a / nav now has 5 links for Manager (Home / Suppliers / Locations / Taxonomy / Items) and 6 for Admin (+ Users).** Approaching the limit of "all links visible at once" before a hamburger / overflow menu is needed. The next nav addition (probably "Stock takes" once ST1 lands, or "Reports" once R1 lands) should trigger a Settings sub-grouping. Defer until then — premature grouping would make the current four settings links *less* discoverable.
- **I1a / no in-form error rendering for items.** Same UX gap as suppliers/locations/taxonomy/field-defs — a 400 lands the user on a bare error page instead of returning to the form with the bad field highlighted. Five forms now share the gap; a single "settings UX polish" slice could fix all five at once. Cost grows linearly with each new form; no individual form is worth fixing in isolation.
- **I1a / no test for the integration of items with the audit-immutability triggers.** `tests/integration/test_audit_immutability.py` exercises the trigger by inserting and trying to UPDATE arbitrary rows. The new `item.*` action vocabulary doesn't break any invariant of the trigger (which doesn't introspect actions), so this is fine — but if the audit-viewer UI (M6 territory) later adds a fixed action allowlist, it'll need every entity type's actions added. Flag for then.
- **S5 / type-change on edit is silent.** `update_field_def` accepts a type change from `text` → `select` (or `select` → `multiselect`, etc.) and just writes the new type. There are no items yet, so this is fine — but once items reference a field def by id and key, a type change silently invalidates every stored value of that field on every existing item. MISSION §3 says "existing items keep their stored values, but new edits to those items must satisfy the current schema" — that's the S6 versioning slice's job to enforce. Don't try to forbid type changes here; the right answer is "warn and let the manager proceed", with item-side migration recorded in the audit log. Note for S6.
- **S5 / `key` is auto-derived from name and not exposed on the form.** Renaming a field whose slug shifts will silently change the key. For S5 this is fine (no items reference fields yet). For I2, the key needs to be either (a) shown on the edit form so the manager sees the consequence, or (b) frozen-after-first-item-references-it. Decision deferred to I2; flag here so the next dev sees it.
- **S5 / leaf invariant on unarchive is symmetric with create, but archive is intentionally NOT.** A field def can be archived even when the node is no longer a leaf (e.g. manager added a sub-cat under a node and now wants to clean up the orphan defs). That's the same posture S4 took for archiving sub-cats under archived parents — cleanup, not new structure. Tested in `test_unarchive_on_non_leaf_node_is_400`.
- **S5 / cross-cutting import**: `app/taxonomy.py` now imports `has_active_field_defs` from `app/field_defs.py`. Direction is one-way (field_defs doesn't import taxonomy), no cycle. But the coupling makes "remove field defs entirely" a multi-file change. Acceptable — the leaf invariant is genuinely cross-cutting.
- **S5 / `options_json` is `list[str]`, not `list[dict]`**. Real selects often want stable values + friendly labels (e.g. value `"18k"` displayed as `"18 carat (gold)"`). v1 doesn't need it; if I2 needs it, the migration is a no-op (already JSON) and only the parser/validator changes. Note for I2.
- **S5 / cascading archive still not implemented.** Archiving a top-level node leaves its field defs active, which is consistent with S4 (archiving doesn't archive sub-cats either). A "settings polish" slice could cascade-archive the schema when a node archives, but only after items reference it (so the cascade has a meaningful trigger). Defer.
- **S5 / route handler param shadows `type` builtin.** `update_field_def(... type: str = Form(""))` shadows the Python builtin within the handler scope. Aesthetically not great; FastAPI uses `type` as the form-key (it's the HTML field name), so renaming would need `Form(..., alias="type")`. The handler doesn't call `type()` so there's no actual risk. Cosmetic; leave.
- **S5 / extraction across 4 settings shapes is now decisively a non-starter.** Field defs adds: a leaf invariant, key auto-derivation, options validation per type, two unique indexes (vs. one elsewhere), an extra leaf-re-check on unarchive. The S4 self-critique called this; S5 is the fifth piece of evidence pointing the same direction. The cheaper fix if drift becomes painful: per-action shared helpers (`_apply_archive(node_or_field, action_name)`), not a router meta-helper. Don't try to extract.
- **S5 / e2e walk has grown to 20 steps in one function (~150 lines).** It's now harder to read end-to-end. If I2 / I3 add more steps to the same flow, split into multiple `test_…` functions sharing a Playwright fixture rather than chaining steps. Note for next iteration that touches `test_taxonomy_e2e.py`.
- **S4 / route-shape duplication has now grown to 14 endpoints in `app/taxonomy.py` alone, and the extraction case has *weakened*, not strengthened.** Sub-cat routes diverge from the top-level shape on multiple axes: parent_id is positional in the URL (top-level routes have no parent), the depth-limit guard is sub-cat-only, the archived-parent guard is sub-cat-create-only, the redirect target depends on parent (`/admin/taxonomy/{parent_id}/children` vs `/admin/taxonomy`), and the audit `after.parent_id` is the parent id (vs `None`). Collapsing top-level + sub-cat into a single helper would need a config object that knows about all five axes; collapsing further across suppliers/locations/taxonomy would compound that. Each route handler is short enough to read top-to-bottom (≤ 30 lines), so the cost of duplication is bounded. Decision: defer extraction indefinitely. Revisit only if a future settings entity adds a *sixth* concrete variant. The cheaper alternative if drift becomes a problem: a per-action shared helper like `_apply_archive(node, message)` that takes a node + the audit action name, leaving the routes thin shells. Not worth doing today.
- **S4 / no cascading archive: archiving a top-level node does not archive its sub-cats.** A manager who archives "Raw Materials" still sees "Silver", "Gold", etc. as active rows on `/admin/taxonomy/{rm.id}/children?show=active`. That's intentionally conservative — items live on leaf nodes, and silently archiving items' classifiers is a data-integrity risk we'd rather make explicit when items exist. Revisit in I1 (when items reference a leaf) or in a dedicated "settings polish" slice. The UX cue today is the "Parent archived" note on the children list saying new sub-cats can't be added — the manager has to archive sub-cats individually if they want a clean cleanup. Acceptable for v1.
- **S4 / depth-limit + archived-parent guards are route-only, not DB-enforced.** A direct INSERT could create a third level (`grandparent.parent_id = parent.id` where `parent.parent_id IS NOT NULL`) or a sub-cat under an archived parent. SQLAlchemy code paths all funnel through the route helpers, so this is a defensive concern about future bugs / migration scripts. A CHECK constraint (`parent_id IS NULL OR (SELECT parent_id FROM taxonomy_nodes WHERE id = parent_id) IS NULL`) is awkward in SQLite (no scalar subqueries in CHECKs); a trigger would work but doubles the maintenance surface. Defer — flag for a hardening pass.
- **S4 / `_get_top_level_parent` returns 400 (depth violation) but `_get_sub_category` returns 404 (not-a-sub-cat).** Slight asymmetry — the first reveals "this id exists but as a sub-cat", the second hides the distinction between "id doesn't exist" and "id exists but as a top-level". Both are reasonable for their respective routes but a future security-conscious reviewer might prefer 404-everywhere to avoid the structural disclosure. Internal admin UI; not a security concern in v1. Document and move on.
- **S4 / `taxonomy_form.html` now serves four shapes** (new top-level, edit top-level, new sub-cat, edit sub-cat) by reading `node` and `parent` from the context. The CTA-text branching (`{% if node %}Save changes{% else %}{% if parent %}Create sub-category{% else %}Create category{% endif %}{% endif %}`) is dense; the next time this template grows, split into per-shape templates rather than nested conditionals.
- ~~**S3 / three concrete settings-CRUD shapes now live side by side (suppliers, locations, taxonomy).** Helper duplication is real but not uniform: taxonomy adds `sort_order` (int parse, blank-on-edit-keeps-existing, default-step-by-10) and a `parent_id is not None → 404` guard on every endpoint. Suppliers and locations don't have either. Collapsing all three into a generic helper now would mean either (a) hard-coding the union of all features (sort_order + email/phone + parent_id guard) into the helper, or (b) building a config-driven registry whose configs are barely simpler than the routes. Wait until S4 (sub-categories) — that slice will reuse `taxonomy_nodes` and either fit the existing shape (one more vote for extraction) or introduce a fourth variant (vote against). Re-evaluate at the end of S4.~~ *Resolved: S4 introduced a fourth variant with multiple new axes (parent_id positional, depth-limit, archived-parent guard, parent-aware redirect). Decision recorded in the new top-of-list S4 entry: defer extraction indefinitely; revisit only if a sixth variant lands.*
- **S3 / sort_order UX is a raw integer input, not a reorder gesture.** MISSION §3 says "Manager can rename, archive, or **reorder** taxonomy nodes". The input technically lets the manager reorder by editing the number, but it's not the natural gesture (drag-drop, up/down arrows). Defer to a UI polish slice once HTMX is actually being used somewhere — the same control will likely apply to suppliers/locations if we add ordering there too. Not blocking S3's DoD progress.
- **S3 / the partial unique indexes rely on SQLite ≥ 3.8 partial-index support.** Pyproject pins Python 3.11+, which on every modern OS ships SQLite ≥ 3.39 (released 2022). `create_engine` doesn't sanity-check the SQLite version, so a pathologically old runtime would silently create non-unique indexes. The risk is theoretical — every macOS / Linux distro from the last 8+ years ships a sufficient SQLite — but worth flagging in case CI ever runs against a stripped container. Cheap fix: a startup-time `PRAGMA compile_options` check, or assert via SQLAlchemy's `dialect.server_version_info`.
- ~~**S3 / sub-category schema is in place but unexercised through routes.**~~ *Resolved in S4: sub-cat routes now exercise the `(parent_id, name)` partial unique index through `_check_child_name_unique`, the depth limit is enforced at the application layer in `_get_top_level_parent` (returns 400 on depth violation), and the same partial unique index covers the new routes' uniqueness checks. Tests in `TestSubCategoryCreate::test_create_under_sub_category_parent_is_400` and `test_create_rejects_duplicate_sibling_name` / `test_create_rejects_duplicate_archived_sibling_name` cover both invariants.*
- ~~**S2 / route + template duplication ... has hit the extraction threshold.**~~ *Partially resolved in S2.5: the `init_templates`/`_t()` plumbing is gone — both routers now import the shared `templates` from `app.template_env` directly. The route-handler helper duplication (`_normalise`/`_validate_name`/`_check_name_unique`/`_diff`/`_flash`) is **deliberately left in place**: collapsing it now would mean inventing a `_FIELDS` registry to drive a generic helper before the third concrete shape (S3 taxonomy) is on the page. Re-evaluate once S3 lands. — **Update (S3):** Now that the third shape is on the page, see the new top-of-list note. The duplication grew non-uniform features (`sort_order`, `parent_id` guard); extraction is now harder, not easier. Wait until S4.*
- **S2.5 / `templates` is now a true module-level singleton.** Tests can't easily swap it for one with different processors. No test today needs that — TestClient uses the real app — but if a future test wants to render a template against a fake processor (e.g. to assert what the processor receives without booting Starlette), it'd have to monkey-patch the module attribute. Acceptable. Flag if/when a test needs it.
- **S2.5 / `app.template_env` test reads `templates.context_processors` directly.** That's a starlette public attribute today (set in `Jinja2Templates.__init__`) but isn't documented as stable surface. The test has a fallback to `templates.env.globals.get("__context_processors__", [])` which is hopeful — if starlette renames the attribute the test will fall through and silently say "no processors". Strictly the test should round-trip: render a tiny `<{{ csrf_token }}|{{ flash }}>` template through `TemplateResponse` and parse the output. Defer until/unless a starlette upgrade actually breaks the current attribute access.
- **S2 / no audit-action coverage for `location.*` in the existing audit-immutability tests.** `tests/integration/test_audit_immutability.py` exercises the trigger by inserting and trying to UPDATE arbitrary rows, which is fine. But it doesn't enumerate the action vocabulary. Adding `location.*` extends the implicit vocabulary; if a future trigger added a CHECK on `action` (it doesn't currently) we'd silently break it. Today this is fine — flagged in case the audit-viewer UI (M6 territory) adds a fixed action allowlist.
- **S2 / inherits S1's UX gaps verbatim.** Bare 400 page on validation failure, no pagination, no e2e on the negative-role path, archived-name conflict message doesn't say *which* row it clashed with. All four are already in this list under the S1 entries; S2 doesn't make any of them worse, but it doubles the cost of fixing each one (now two routes have to be updated, soon three). When the "settings UX polish" slice lands, do all the routers in one pass.
- **S1 / validation failures show a bare 400 page, not the form re-rendered with errors.** A user submits an empty name and gets "name is required" as a stark FastAPI HTTPException page instead of the form with the field highlighted. Mirrors the existing `admin_users` route convention but isn't great UX. The `suppliers_form.html` template already takes a `form` dict and renders submitted values, so the upgrade is small: swap `HTTPException(400, ...)` for `templates.TemplateResponse(..., status_code=400, ...)` with an `errors` dict. Defer to a "settings UX polish" slice (after S2/S3 land so the change covers all settings forms at once).
- **S1 / no email format validation.** Browser `type="email"` validates client-side but not server-side. Storing garbage emails will bite at PO send time (PO5). MISSION says "boring is good" — defer to a single validation point at PO5 (cheaper than re-validating everywhere).
- **S1 / DoD #9 has integration coverage but not e2e coverage on the negative path.** Workshop=403, Office=403, anonymous=401 are exhaustively integration-tested for `/admin/suppliers`. The e2e only covers the positive path (manager succeeds). Strictly the DoD says "verified by tests" (plural, not specifically e2e). I'm leaving #9 unticked for now — being conservative; consider in the next iteration whether to (a) tick as-is, or (b) add a one-liner e2e that has a workshop user navigate to `/admin/suppliers` and assert a 403 page renders. Cheap addition.
- **S1 / no pagination on the suppliers list.** The list view renders every active or archived row inline. UC has tens of suppliers, not thousands, so this is fine for v1. Worth flagging because the same template will be cloned for items (I1+), where 5000 rows IS realistic. Don't copy the bare-list pattern there.
- **S1 / archived names share the namespace with active names.** Tested + intentional: archiving doesn't free the name. Operator must rename the old row or unarchive it. The 400 message ("a supplier with that name already exists") doesn't tell the user *which* one — confusing if the conflict is with an archived supplier they don't see by default. Defer to a UX polish slice.
- **F4 / CSRF doesn't cover multipart bodies.** `_extract_submitted_token` reads only `application/x-www-form-urlencoded`. Multipart form-posts (file uploads — not yet a feature) must send the token in the `X-CSRF-Token` header instead, or they'll fail CSRF. When the first upload route lands (likely with item photos or PO PDFs), either extend the middleware to parse multipart or document the header requirement explicitly on those routes. Captured in the docstring of `app/csrf.py` so the next dev sees it.
- ~~**F4 / no flash-message region in the layout.**~~ *Resolved in S1: `_flash_context_processor` registered on `Jinja2Templates`, base layout renders `<div class="flash" role="status" data-testid="flash">` when `request.session["flash"]` is set; supplier mutations populate it. Tested in `tests/integration/test_layout.py::TestFlashRegion`.*
- ~~**F4 / nav for active non-admin users renders just "Home".**~~ *Partially resolved in S1: Manager + Admin now also see "Suppliers". Workshop and Office still see only "Home" until M2 (stock-in form) and SC1 (scan-mode page) land.*
- **F4 / CSRF token doesn't rotate on login or logout.** Same token persists across sign-in/sign-out cycles for as long as the cookie lives. Threat model says fine: SameSite=Lax + non-HttpOnly-but-same-origin means a cross-site attacker can't read or set the cookie. The window where this matters is a session-fixation-style attack where attacker plants a known csrftoken cookie in the victim's browser before login — they can't, because they can't write our domain's cookies cross-site. Document and move on.
- **F4 / HTMX is loaded but unused.** No route emits HTML fragments yet. The `<script>` tag is there for the next slice to start using; the integrity hash pins us to 1.9.12 — bumping requires updating both the URL and the SRI.
- **F3 / no audit-viewer UI.** Today the audit log is observable only via direct DB access. That's enough for tests and for an eyeball on a dev DB, but for "Manager can see who has what" / "Admin can investigate an incident" we'll need a real `/admin/audit` (or per-entity timeline) view. Belongs alongside the item-detail timeline (M6 territory) — building it earlier means rendering rows for actions that don't exist yet. Not blocking DoD #8.
- **F3 / returning-user name/email refresh is silent.** `upsert_user_from_userinfo` updates `email`/`name` from Google on every sign-in but writes no audit row, so a Google-side rename is invisible. Strict reading of "every state-changing action" suggests a `user.profile_synced` row should be written when Google's payload differs from what's stored. Cheap fix (adds 5 lines + a test), can land in F4 or later.
- **F3 / migration → trigger linkage isn't tested end-to-end.** `apply_immutability_triggers` is exercised by unit tests that install it themselves; the migration does call it on `op.get_bind()`, but no test asserts that running `alembic upgrade head` against a clean DB produces tamper-proof tables. The e2e suite runs the migration but never tries to UPDATE/DELETE audit rows. Risk: a future refactor drops the trigger call, tests stay green, prod is silently unprotected. Mitigate with a small "post-migration tamper test" — run `alembic upgrade head` against a temp SQLite, attempt UPDATE, expect failure.
- **F3 / Postgres path is implemented but untested.** The `plpgsql` block-function + triggers are written but no CI run exercises them. Acceptable for v1 — covered when P3 (Postgres parity) lands. Worth a sanity-read before that slice.
- ~~**F2.1 / still no CSRF on POSTs, and now there are real ones.**~~ *Resolved in F4: `CSRFMiddleware` with double-submit cookie now gates every state-changing route except the two intentional exemptions (`/auth/google/callback`, `/auth/_dev-login`). Tested in `tests/integration/test_csrf.py`.*
- **F2.1 / no last-admin guard.** Server prevents an admin from demoting/disabling *themselves*, but not from demoting/disabling another admin — including the only other admin. Sequence to lock everyone out: A and B are admins; A demotes B to manager (allowed), then disables themselves... no, that's blocked. But: A demotes B *and* disables themselves... still blocked on self-disable. Genuine lock-out path: A demotes themselves (blocked), so really just: A disables B → A leaves → no one can manage. Recovery requires direct DB access or wiping admins so the bootstrap path re-fires. Not blocking, but worth a 30-line slice ("cannot remove the last active admin") soon.
- ~~**F2.1 / `/auth/me` doesn't enforce status.**~~ *Resolved in F4: `/auth/me` now depends on `require_active_user`, which 403s any non-active user (pending or disabled) even with a valid cookie. Tested in `tests/integration/test_auth_routes.py::TestAuthMe::test_disabled_user_with_valid_session_is_403` and `::test_pending_user_with_valid_session_is_403`.*
- ~~**F2 / no CSRF on POSTs.**~~ *Resolved in F4. `/auth/logout` now requires CSRF; `/auth/_dev-login` remains intentionally exempt as documented in `app/csrf.py` (it's a non-prod-only backdoor and CSRF on a backdoor protects nothing).*
- **F2 / dev-login backdoor exists in `dev` too, not just `test`.** Useful for local hacking, but it is a real backdoor: anyone who can reach the dev server can sign in as anyone. Document this in the README (done) and consider tightening to `test`-only (or requiring an env-var token) once we have a real dev workflow.
- **F2 / migration's CHECK constraint duplicates the enum members.** `migrations/versions/0001_create_users.py` hard-codes `('admin','manager','office','workshop')` and `('pending','active','disabled')`. Adding a new `Role` member without a migration update would silently make the model accept values the DB rejects. Tests would catch it (any insert with the new value would fail), but consider dropping the CHECK in favour of just trusting the SAEnum, or generating the constraint from the enum at migration time.
- ~~**F2 / no audit on user creation/promotion.**~~ *Resolved in F3: `upsert_user_from_userinfo` now writes `user.created` (+ `user.bootstrap_admin_granted` for the seed admin path), tested in `tests/integration/test_audit_routes.py::TestUpsertUserAudit`.*
- ~~**F2 / templates lack accessibility polish.**~~ *Resolved in F4: skip-link, visible focus ring, `aria-current="page"` on the active nav item, larger tap targets. Tested in `tests/integration/test_layout.py::TestBaseLayoutAccessibility`. Future passes (P2 in the backlog) can audit deeper (contrast ratios, screen-reader walk-through, etc.) once there are more pages.*
- **F1 / e2e fixture readiness probe (carried).** `tests/e2e/conftest.py` still uses TCP-port-open as readiness. Hasn't flaked in F2; revisit only if it does.

## Decisions log

*(Non-trivial implementation decisions worth remembering. One line each. Helps future iterations not re-litigate settled choices.)*

- **Alembic env.py reads `DATABASE_URL` from `app.config.settings`**, not from `alembic.ini`. Single source of truth across dev/prod, and means `alembic` invocations honour `.env` automatically.
- **`render_as_batch=True` on SQLite** in `migrations/env.py` so future ALTER TABLE migrations work on SQLite (which doesn't support most ALTER ops natively). Postgres ignores the flag.
- **e2e fixture spawns a real uvicorn subprocess** rather than using ASGI in-process. Trades startup cost (~2s) for fidelity to the production transport. Acceptable while the e2e suite is small.
- **e2e suite uses an isolated temp SQLite file + runs `alembic upgrade head` before booting uvicorn** (rather than `Base.metadata.create_all`), so e2e exercises the actual migration path. This is what caught the enum-name-vs-value mismatch in F2.
- **Enum columns store enum values, not names** — `SAEnum(..., values_callable=lambda cls: [e.value for e in cls])`. Without this, SAEnum stores the Python member name (e.g. `"PENDING"`) which doesn't match our migration's lowercase CHECK constraints. Apply the same `values_callable` to every future enum column.
- **Users use a separate `status` enum (pending/active/disabled) and a *nullable* `role`**, rather than overloading role with a `pending` value. Reason: status is orthogonal to role — a Manager can be temporarily disabled without losing their assigned role. This costs one column and keeps the role enum honest.
- **Bootstrap admin promotion is one-shot.** Once any admin exists, `BOOTSTRAP_ADMIN_EMAIL` matches no longer auto-promote. Without this, leaving the env var set in prod would silently grant admin to anyone matching it on first sign-in.
- **`require_role` blocks pending and disabled users even if their role would otherwise match.** Status overrides role for access decisions. Tested explicitly so future refactors don't quietly weaken this.
- **Dev-login backdoor `POST /auth/_dev-login`** is mounted in `dev` and `test` only, gated by `settings.app_env`. Used by the Playwright suite (and local dev) to sign in without a real Google round-trip. Hard-disabled in prod by the env check at module import + a redundant runtime check inside the handler.
- **`record_audit` flushes inside the caller's transaction; the caller commits.** The audit row and the change it records succeed-or-fail together. Helper never commits — that's a deliberate constraint so a future bug can't half-commit a state change without its log entry.
- **`actor=user` for `user.created`** (not `actor=None`). The user is treated as the actor of their own first-time creation; the bootstrap admin promotion is logged as a separate `actor=None` system event. Rationale: keeps every "user-initiated" event attributable to a human, even when the human is the subject.
- **Audit log immutability is enforced at the DB layer.** SQLite uses `BEFORE UPDATE`/`BEFORE DELETE` triggers with `RAISE(ABORT, 'audit_log is append-only: …')`; Postgres uses an equivalent `plpgsql` function. The trigger SQL lives in `app/audit.py` so the migration and any test fixture share one source of truth (`apply_immutability_triggers`).
- **CSRF uses double-submit cookie, not session-stored token.** Token lives in a non-HttpOnly `csrftoken` cookie + a matching `csrf_token` form field or `X-CSRF-Token` header. Reasoning: the session cookie is encrypted/signed and not readable by tests/JS, which would force every caller to first parse the rendered HTML to discover the token. Double-submit makes the token discoverable to legitimate callers (HTMX, fetch, Playwright) while `SameSite=Lax` keeps the cookie out of cross-site requests.
- **CSRF middleware runs outside SessionMiddleware.** `CSRFMiddleware` is added second in `app/main.py` so it's the *outermost* middleware. Forged requests get rejected before SessionMiddleware ever decodes the session cookie. Cost: anonymous forged POSTs return 403 before authentication runs, which is why `test_unauthenticated_post_is_401` has to bootstrap a CSRF cookie first.
- **`/auth/_dev-login` is CSRF-exempt by design.** The dev-login backdoor is mounted only in `dev`/`test`. Adding CSRF to a backdoor that bypasses real auth would only add ceremony, not security — anyone who can reach the dev server already has full access. This is documented in `app/csrf.py::DEFAULT_EXEMPT_PATHS` so the next dev doesn't quietly "fix" it.
- **`require_active_user` is a separate dependency from `require_role`.** Pre-F4, `require_user` only checked "is there a user?" and `require_role` checked status as a side-effect. Routes that don't have role gating but should still reflect current account state (today: `/auth/me`) need their own status check — added as `require_active_user`. Without it, a user disabled mid-session continues to read their own profile via a still-valid cookie until they sign out.
- **Suppliers (and other Manager-owned settings) live under `/admin/...`** even though "admin" in the URL implies the admin role. Reasoning: the existing `/admin/users` set the `admin` prefix as "admin/settings area," not strictly "admin role." The role gate is in the dependency (`require_role(Role.MANAGER)` for suppliers, `require_role(Role.ADMIN)` for users), not the URL. Don't read the URL prefix as a role signal.
- **Suppliers `name` is unique across active *and* archived rows.** Archiving does not free the name. To re-use a name the operator must rename the existing row or unarchive it. Reason: PO history and FIFO layers may reference a supplier by id, but humans reference by name; allowing two "Acme Wax Co" rows (one archived, one active) would silently let the wrong one feed reorder math. Tested at the DB layer (`uq_suppliers_name`) and at the route layer (`_check_name_unique`).
- **No-op POSTs (update with no field changes, archive an already-archived supplier, unarchive an active one) write no audit row but still 303 to the list.** Reason: tests assert this explicitly so a future refactor doesn't accidentally start logging spurious "X updated" rows that drown the real signal. The 303 still happens so the browser's POST-redirect-GET cycle terminates cleanly.
- **`record_audit` for `supplier.updated` records *only* the changed fields, not the full row.** `_diff()` returns a sparse `(before, after)` of fields whose value changed. Reason: full-row before/after gets noisy fast (especially with `notes`), and the DoD requirement is that "every state change is attributable" — knowing exactly what changed beats a lossy snapshot of everything.
- **Flash messages live in `request.session["flash"]` and are popped (read+clear) by `flash_context_processor` on render.** One-shot semantics: appears on the next page render, never on the one after. Tested in `test_layout.py::TestFlashRegion::test_flash_appears_after_set_then_cleared_on_next_load` and `tests/unit/test_template_env.py::TestFlashContextProcessor`. Don't try to "tag" flashes with a type (success/warning/etc.) until there's a real second type to render — current uses are all success messages.
- **The shared `Jinja2Templates` instance lives in `app.template_env` as a module global.** Every router (today: `app.main`, `app.suppliers`, `app.locations`; tomorrow: taxonomy + items + everything else) imports `templates` from there. Reason: the app needs a single Jinja env so the CSRF + flash context processors are guaranteed to be present on every render — a router building its own `Jinja2Templates` would silently drop both. Module-level is fine because the configuration is pure (template directory + two pure-function processors). *(Supersedes the earlier "`app.suppliers.init_templates()` shim" decision from S1.)*
